### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 41 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is:
Choices:
  A: Rs. 697.50
  B: Rs. 712.50
  C: Rs. 787.50
  D: Rs. 750
  E: Rs. 780
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let C be the cost price of the watch.
  Let D be the originally applied discount of 5%.
  Applying a D% discount to an item reduces its price by D%.
  Therefore, a selling price after a D% discount is (100 - D)% of the original price.
  The shopkeeper earns a profit when the selling price is greater than the cost price.
  The profit earned on selling a watch at a price P after the discount is (P - C).
  The profit earned on selling a watch at a price P after the discount of D% is ((100 - D)P/100 - C).
 
Calculation:
  Let M be the marked price of the watch.
  When a discount of 5% is applied, the selling price is 95% of the marked price, i.e. (95/100)M.
  When a discount of 7% is applied, the selling price is 93% of the marked price, i.e. (93/100)M.
  According to the problem, (93/100)M - C = (95/100)M - C - 15.
  Simplifying the equation, we get (2/100)M = 15, or M = 750.
 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Let's assume the marked price of the watch be "x".
Then he gave a discount of 5%, so the selling price is (95/100)*x.
In this case, the profit made by the shopkeeper is (95/100)*x - C1, where C1 is the cost price of the watch.
Now, he gave a discount of 7%, so the new selling price is (93/100)*x.
In this case, the profit made by the shopkeeper is (93/100)*x - (C1+15).
We can create an equation based on the above information, as follows:
(95/100)*x - C1 = (93/100)*x - (C1+15)
Solving this equation, we get C1 = (100*15)/2 = 750.
So, the cost price of the watch is Rs. 750.
Now we can calculate the marked price of the watch:
Marked Price = Cost Price / (100 - % Discount)
Using this formula, we can find the marked price as follows:
Marked Price = 750 / (1 - 5/100) = Rs. 787.50
Therefore, the answer is (C) Rs. 787.50.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Let's assume that the marked price of the watch is MP.
  A discount of 5% means a selling price of 95% of the marked price (0.95*MP).
  Similarly, a discount of 7% means a selling price of 93% of the marked price (0.93*MP).
  The shopkeeper's profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price (CP).
  If the shopkeeper's profit is Rs. X, then we can say that:
  0.95*MP - CP = X  (using 5% discount)
  0.93*MP - CP = X + 15  (using 7% discount and Rs. 15 less profit)

Calculation:
  We can solve the above system of equations to get the value of MP.
  Subtracting the second equation from the first, we get:
  0.02*MP = 15
  MP = 750

M = (15 * 100) / 2 = 750

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 43 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is:
Choices:
  A: 2.6m
  B: 3.9m
  C: 4m
  D: 4.2m
  E: 4.4m
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- The semi-perimeter of a room is half the sum of the lengths of its four walls.
- The cost of papering the walls of a room can be calculated by finding the perimeter of the room (by doubling its semi-perimeter), subtracting the area of doors and windows, and using this value to determine the amount of paper needed to cover the walls.
- The ratio of the height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5.

Let the height of the room be 2x, and the semi-perimeter be 5x. This means that each of the shorter walls has length x, and each of the longer walls has length 2x.

The perimeter of the room is then 2(2x) + 2(x) = 6x. 

After subtracting the area of the doors and windows (15 sq.m), we have 6x * H = (6x*2/100) * Rs.2 * (100-15), where H is the height of the room in meters. 

Solving this equation, we get H = 4 meters.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  1. Semi-perimeter of a room = (1/2) * (sum of all sides). 
  2. Let's assume that the height of the room is '2x' and the semi-perimeter is '5y'. So, we can write the following equations:
        - 2x/5y = 2/5 => x = (2/5)y. 
        - Cost of papering the walls = Cost of the paper * Length of paper required. 
  3. The area of the room = Length * Height = (5y/2) * 2x = 5xy.
  4. The area of the doors and windows = 15 sq.m. So, the area of the walls = 5xy - 15.
  5. The length of paper required = 2 * (height + length of the longer wall) = 4x + 5y.
  6. Substituting x = (2/5)y in the above equation, we get length of paper required = (18/5)y. 

Calculation: 
  1. Cost of papering the walls = Rs. 260, Cost of the paper = Rs. 2/meter, Area of doors and windows = 15 sq.m.
  2. So, Length of paper required = (5xy - 15)/(50/100) = (10*(5xy - 15))/50 = 2(5xy - 15) meters.
  3. Cost of papering the walls = cost of the paper * Length of paper required. So, we have:
            260 = 2 * (2(5xy - 15)) => 260 = 20xy - 60 => 20xy = 320. 
  4. Substituting the value of x = (2/5)y in the above equation, we get: 
            20*(2/5)y^2 = 320 => y^2 = 80 => y = 4 sqrt(5).
  5. Height of the room = 2x = 2 * (2/5)y = (4/5)y = (4/5) * 4 sqrt(5) = 16 sqrt(5)/5.
      
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  Semi-perimeter = (Perimeter of Room) / 2
  Paper needed for the wall = Room area - Area of doors and windows

  Then the semi-perimeter of the room = (Perimeter) / 2= (2x + b + b)/2 = x+b
  By the ratio, we can conclude that the breadth of the room is 5x/2
  Area of the four walls of the room = Perimeter * Height = (2 x (2x + 5x/2)) * 2x = 9x^2
  From the total area of the four walls, we can subtract the area of doors and windows to get the area of the walls that need to be papered.
  Length of the paper used = (Area of walls to be papered) / (Width of paper) = (9x^2 - 15) / 0.5 = 18x^2 - 30
  Cost of paper = Length of paper used x Price per meter of paper = (18x^2 - 30) x 2
  Total cost = Rs.260

   2h(5x - 2x) + 2h(2x) where h is the height of the room.

   Substituting the value of 16hx from the first equation, we get

   Simplifying the above equation we get 4hx = 25h - 59.
   
The cost of papering the walls is given as Rs.260 and the total area of the walls is:
   2h(5x - 2x) + 2h(2x) - 15 = 2h(3x) = 6hx
   Since the paper is 50cm wide, or 0.5m wide, the length of paper required is 6hx / 0.5 = 12hx
   So, the cost of papering the walls is Rs.2 per meter, or Rs.0.20 per decimeter (1 meter = 10 decimeters).
   Therefore, the cost of papering the walls is 12hx * Rs.0.20/dm = 2.4hx
   
Substituting the value of 4hx from the second equation, we get 25h - 59 = 2.4h
Solving for h gives us h = 4.2m

Therefore, the height of the room is 4.2m, which corresponds to option D.

Action: Answer("C")  
To solve this problem, we can use the following steps:
Let the height of the room be 2x.
Let the semi-perimeter of the room be 5y.
Then, the four sides of the room are 5y/2, 2x, 5y/2, and 2x.
The perimeter of the room is 5y + 4x.
We know that the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5.
So, we have 2x/5y = 2/5.
Simplifying this equation, we get x/y = 1/5.
The area of the four walls is (5y/2 + 2x) * (5y/2) = 25y^2/4 + 5yx.
The cost of covering the walls with paper is Rs.260 for an area of (25y^2/4 + 5yx) * 2.
So, Rs.260 = 2 * (25y^2/4 + 5yx) * 0.02.
Simplifying this equation, we get y^2 + 2yx = 260/2 = 130.
We also know that the area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m.
So, (5y/2) * 2x = area of doors and windows + area of the walls.
Substituting the value of x/y from earlier, we get:
(5y/2) * (2/5y) = 15 + 25y^2/4 + 5yx.
Simplifying this equation, we get 5y^2 + 4yx = 120.
Now we have two equations:
y^2 + 2yx = 130
5y^2 + 4yx = 120
Multiplying the first equation by 2, we get:
2y^2 + 4yx = 260
Subtracting the second equation from this, we get:
-3y^2 = 140
y^2 = -140/3 (which is not possible)
Therefore, there is no solution to this problem. Hence, 'none of the above' is the most likely answer. So the answer would be C: None of the above.

  Semi-perimeter of a room is half of the sum of its four sides.

Action: Answer("C") 

Let the height of the room be 2x, then the semi-perimeter of the room is (5/2)x.

Let the length and breadth of the room be l and b respectively.

Then we have

l + b = (5/2)x

2(l + b) = 5x

l + b = (5/2)x

We need to find the height 2x.

Area of the four walls = Height x (Length + Breadth) = 2x (l + b)

Area covered by doors and windows = 15 sq.m

Area of the remaining walls = 2x (l + b) - 15

Area of paper required = Total area of walls + Doors and windows - Area of uncovered parts

Area of paper required = 2x (l + b) + 15 - 2x (l + b)/5

Area of paper required = 2x (l + b) + 15 - 2/5 (5/2)x (l + b)

Area of paper required = 2x (l + b) + 15 - x (l + b)

Area of paper required = (x + 15) (l + b)

Cost of papering the walls = Rs.260

Cost of papering the walls = Cost of paper required

260 = (x + 15) (l + b) x 2

130 = (x + 15) (l + b) x 1

130 = (x + 15) (5x/2) / 2

52 = (x + 15) x 5x / 4

52 x 4 / 5 = x^2 + 15x

x^2 + 15x - 41.6 = 0

Solving for x, we get x = 4

Therefore, the height of the room is 2x = 8m. 

Hence, the answer is C: 4m.

  Let's denote the length, breadth and height of the room as l, b, and h respectively.
  The total area of the four walls of the room is 2h(l+b) and after subtracting the area of the windows and doors, the area of the walls that need to be papered is 2h(l+b) - 15.
Action: Answer("D")  
Solution: 
  Let x be the common ratio between height and semi-perimeter. Then, the height of the room is 2x and its semi-perimeter is 5x.
  We know that cost of papering the walls is Rs.260. We also know that the cost of paper, which is Rs.2 per meter, is equivalent to the cost of papering 1 square meter of area. Since the width of the paper is 0.5m, we can say that the cost of papering 1 square meter of area is Rs.4.
  Therefore, the area of the walls that need to be papered is 260/4 = 65 sq.m.
  We can now set up two equations:
  2h(l+b) - 15 = 65    (1)
  h/l+b = 2/5          (2)
  Simplifying equation (2), we get h = 2l/5 + 2b/5
  Substituting the value of h in equation (1), we get:
  2(2l/5 + 2b/5)(l+b) - 15 = 65
  Simplifying this equation and solving for l, we get l=6.5.
  Substituting l=6.5 in equation (2) and solving for h, we get h=4.2m.
  Hence, the height of the room is 4.2m (Option D)

Solution:
Let the height of the room be 2x and its semi-perimeter be 5x. 

The perimeter of the room is 2 times the semi-perimeter, which is 10x. 
Therefore, the width of the room is (10x - 2(2x))/2 = 3x. 

The area of the four walls is (height + width) × perimeter. 
= (2x + 3x) x 10x = 50x²
The area of the doors and windows is 15 sq.m 
∴ The area of the walls = 50x² - 15

The length of paper required would be the circumference of the room, which is equal to the perimeter of the room. 

But each roll is only 50 cm wide, or 0.5 meters. So we need to divide the perimeter by 0.5 to get the number of rolls required. 

The cost of the paper required would be the length of paper required multiplied by Rs. 2 per meter. 
So, the total cost is equal to 2 × (10x/0.5) = 40x 

We have: 
        40x = 260 + (50x² - 15) × 2 
     => 40x = 260 + 100x² - 30 
     => 100x² + 10x - 115 = 0 

Solving this quadratic equation, we get:
        x = sqrt(23)/10 
        height = 2x = 2(sqrt(23)/10)

Knowledge:
  To solve this problem, we need to use geometric formulas for the area and perimeter of a rectangle. 
  We also need to use ratios to calculate the height of the room.

Let x be the width of the room, y be the height of the room, and z be the length of the room.
The perimeter of the room is 2(x + y) + 2(x + z) = 2x + 2y + 2z.
The semi-perimeter of the room is (2x + 2y + 2z)/2 = x + y + z.
The area of the walls is (2x + 2y) * z = 2xz + 2yz.
We are also given that the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5, which means y/(x+y+z) = 2/5.

Action: 
First, we need to find the values of x, y, and z.
From y/(x+y+z) = 2/5, we know that y = 2/5 (x+y+z).
Substituting this into the area equation, we get 2xz + 2yz = 2y(x+y+z)/2 = y(x+y+z).
Rearranging the equation, we get 2xz = yz - xy - y^2
We can use the cost equation to solve for x and z.
The area of the walls is (2x + 2y) * z = 2xz + 2yz = y(x+y+z).
The area of the windows and doors is 15 sq.m.
The total area is the area of the walls minus the area of the windows and doors.
Total area = 2xz + 2yz - 15
Total cost = Total area * cost per unit area = (2xz + 2yz - 15) * 2
260 = (2xz + 2yz - 15) * 2
130 = xz + yz - 7.5

We can now use substitutions to solve for y.
From y/(x+y+z) = 2/5, we know that y = 2/5 (x+y+z).
Substituting this into the equation above, we get:
130 = xz + 2/5 (x+y+z) z - 7.5
215 = 5xz + 2z(x+y+z)
215 = 5xz + 2z(x+3/5z)
215 = z(5x + 13/5z)
Substituting 2xz = yz - xy - y^2, we get:
215 = z(5x + 13/5z) = z(5x + 13/5(yz - xy - y^2))
215 = z(5x + 13/5(y(x+y+z) - xy - y^2))
215 = z(5x + 13/5(yz - y^2))
215 = z(5x + 13/5z(2/5z))
215 = z(5x + 26/25z^2)
215 = 5xz + 26/25z^2
Substituting 130 into the last equation to solve for z:
215 = 5xz + 26/25z^2
215 = 5x(130 - yz + xy + y^2)/(2y) + 26/25(130 - yz + xy + y^2)^2/(4y^2)
Simplifying and solving, we get:
y = 4m

Question: A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is
Choices:
  A: 4 1/3 km/h
  B: 7 2/3 km/h
  C: 9 ½ km/h
  D: 8 km/h
  E: 81 km/h
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Average Speed = Total Distance Covered / Total Time Taken
  Speed = Distance / Time
  To find the answer, we need to find the total distance covered and the total time taken.

Calculations:
  Distance covered at 5 kmph in 6 hrs = 5 kmph * 6 hrs = 30 km
  Distance covered at 4 kmph in 12 hrs = 4 kmph * 12 hrs = 48 km
  Total Distance Covered = 30 km + 48 km = 78 km
  Total Time Taken = 6 hrs + 12 hrs = 18 hrs
  Average Speed = Total Distance Covered / Total Time Taken = 78 km / 18 hrs = 13/3 kmph

Action: Answer("A")  
The average speed of the man is 4 1/3 km/h.

  Total time taken = 6 + 12 = 18 hours

Choices:

The equation can be factored into (x+y)(x-y) = 256000
From the second sentence we know that x+y=1000.
We can use these two equations to solve for x and y.

Calculation:

So we can use this to solve for x-y as follows:
x+y=1000
x-y=(256000)/(x+y)
Now we can solve for x and y using the two equations:
x+y=1000
x-y=512
Solving for x and y we get:
x = (1000+512)/2 = 756
y = (1000-512)/2 = 244

Therefore, the answer is A: 600, 400.

  y = (a-b)/2 = (1000-256)/2 = 372

  (1) x^2 - y^2 = 256000  =>  (x+y)(x-y) = 256000
  (2) x + y = 1000 

We can use these two equations to solve for the values of x and y. 

We can try to find 2 numbers whose product is 256000 and whose sum is 1000.
 
256000 = 2^8 * 5^4
Factors: 1, 2, 4, 5, 8, 10, 16, 20, 25, 32, 40, 50, 64, 80, 100, 125, 160, 200, 250, 320, 400, 500, 800, 1000, 1250, 1600, 2000, 2500, 4000, 5000, 8000, 10000, 20000, 40000, 80000, 160000, 256000

From the above factors, we notice that 500 * 512 = 256000. 
Also, 500 + 512 = 1012. But our sum should be 1000. This suggests that our two numbers are slightly less than 500 and 512. 

Let's try x = 500 and y = 512. 

Then,
x^2 - y^2 = 256000  =>  500^2 - 512^2  = -14412 (incorrect)
However, if we try x = 512 and y = 500, then we get: 
x^2 - y^2 = 256000  =>  512^2 - 500^2 = 14412
That's correct!

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 50 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A starts travel towards south 3km, then travel 5 km towards east, and again travels 3 km to north, and finally travels 2km towards west. In the end how far from is A from home?
Choices:
  A: 3km
  B: 2km
  C: 4km
  D: 5km
  E: 6km
Response 0:
Knowledge: We can find the distance between two points by using the Pythagorean theorem, which states that in a right triangle, the square of the hypotenuse (the longest side) is equal to the sum of the squares of the other two sides. A right triangle is formed by the southward and northward movements, and the eastward and westward movements. 

Action: 
The southward and northward movements cancel out each other.
The eastward and westward movements also cancel out each other.
Therefore, the only distance traveled by A from the beginning point is the hypotenuse of the right triangle formed by the other 4 movements.
The distance between the starting point and the end point is the square root of (5^2 + 3^2) = sqrt(25+9) = sqrt(34) ~ 5.8 km
So, A is about 5.8 km away from home.
Answer: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  This question is about finding the net displacement of A.
  Displacement is the distance between the initial and final points, in a straight line.
  We can use the Pythagorean theorem to find the net displacement.
  Pythagorean theorem states that, in a right angle triangle, the square of the length of the hypotenuse (the longest side) is equal to the sum of the square of the other two sides.
  So, if we know the length of two sides of a right angle triangle, we can find the length of the third side (the hypotenuse).
  
Working:
  The 3 km north and 3 km south distances cancel each other out.
  The 2 km west distance and 5 km east distances cancel each other out as well.
  So the only remaining distance is 4 km east. 
  Therefore, the net displacement is 4 km towards east.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  When the person travels in the north or south direction, the movements to the east and west cannot affect the distance from the starting point. Similarly, when the person travels in the east or west direction, the movements to the north and south cannot affect the distance from the starting point.
  Here the person has traveled 3km south, and then 3km north, so these two movements cancel each other out. Similarly, the person has traveled 5km east, and then 2km west, so these two movements cancel each other out. Therefore, the only movement that matters is the distance between the starting point and the final point, which is a straight line.

Knowledge: To solve this problem, we need to find the net displacement of A from the starting point.

Topic: Math
Question: What should come in place of the question mark(?) in each of the following questions ?
a2 - b2/(a + b)2 (?)=(a - b)2
Choices:
  A: (a + b)(a - b)
  B: (a - b)2
  C: (a + b)2
  D: a3 + b3
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The given expression is a2 - b2/(a + b)2
  The required expression is (a - b)2
 
(a + b)2 = a2 + 2ab + b2
(a - b)2 = a2 - 2ab + b2
(a + b)(a - b) = a2 - b2
 
Therefore, (a - b)2 = a2 - 2ab + b2 = a2 - b2 + 2ab
 
We observe that:
a2 - b2/(a + b)2 = [(a2 - b2) + 2ab]/(a + b)2 = (a - b)2
 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  a2 - b2 = (a-b)(a+b)
  (a-b)2 = a2 - 2ab + b2
  (a + b)2 = a2 + 2ab + b2
  
To solve this problem, we can substitute the above identities in the given equation.

(a-b)(a+b)/(a+b)2 = (a-b)2

(a-b) cancels out on both sides, giving us:

(a+b)/(a+b) = a-b

We can simplify this equation further:

1 = a-b

So, the correct answer is (B) (a - b)2.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  a2 - b2 can be factorized as (a+b)(a-b).
  
  If we multiply (a-b)2 using the formula (a-b)(a-b), we get (a-b)2 = a2 - 2ab + b2. 
  
  If we expand (a+b)2 using the formula (a+b)(a+b), we get (a+b)2 = a2 + 2ab + b2.

  So, (a+b)(a-b)/(a + b)2 = (a-b)2/(a + b) = (a2 - 2ab + b2)/(a2 + 2ab + b2)
  
  So, a2 - b2/(a + b)2 = (a-b)2/(a + b) if and only if a2 - 2ab + b2 = a2 - b2, which is true if we simplify it.

  A: (a + b)(a - b) does not match the derived equation.
  B: (a - b)2 matches the derived equation.
  C: (a + b)2 does not match the derived equation.
  D: a3 + b3 does not match the derived equation.

  => a² - b² / (a + b)² = (a + b)(a - b) / (a + b)²   (Dividing both sides by (a + b)²)

  => (a - b) = ±1

  Therefore, the answer is (a + b)² = (a² + 2ab + b²) = (a + b)² = (c).

  A: 20
  B: 30
  C: 40
  D: 200
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  M = abc is a three digit number, where a, b, and c are digits.
  N = cba is a three digit number, where a, b, and c are digits.
  M > N implies that a > c or a = c and b > c.
  M - N can be simplified to 99(a-c) + 9(b-a), which is a two-digit number whose digits differ by (a-c).
  396c can be simplified to 4c x 99, 3c x 2 x 66, or 11 x 6 x 6c, which is divisible by 99.
  Therefore, 990 is divisible by 99, and M - N + 396c is divisible by 99 as well.

  If a = 3, we must have b > 0, so there are 9 possible values of b, giving a total of 9 x 1 = 9 possible values of M.
  If a = 4, we can have any value of b, so there are 10 possible values of b, giving a total of 10 x 1 = 10 possible values of M.
  If a = 5, we can have any value of b, so there are 10 possible values of b, giving a total of 10 x 1 = 10 possible values of M.
  If a = 6, we can have any value of b, so there are 10 possible values of b, giving a total of 10 x 1 = 10 possible values of M.
  If a = 7, we can have any value of b, so there are 10 possible values of b, giving a total of 10 x 1 = 10 possible values of M.
  If a = 8, we can have any value of b, so there are 10 possible values of b, giving a total of 10 x 1 = 10 possible values of M.
  If a = 9, we can have any value of b, so there are 10 possible values of b, giving a total of 10 x 1 = 10 possible values of M.
  
  Therefore, the total number of possible values of M that are more than 300 is 9 + 10 + 10 + 10 + 10 + 10 + 10 = 69.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 8:
Knowledge:
  The numbers M = abc and N = cba are the reverse of each other, in other words, N is formed by reversing the digits of M.
  Since M is a three-digit number, we have a, b and c are digits between 0 and 9. 
  300 is the smallest three-digit number that is bigger than 300.

Solution:
  Let us denote each digit of M and N as follows:
  M = 100a + 10b + c
  N = 100c + 10b + a
  Then we have:
  M - N = 99a - 99c = 99(a - c) > 0     (since M > N)
  M - N + 396c = 99(a - c) + 396c = 99(a - c + 4c) = 99(a + 3c)
  Therefore, 99(a + 3c) = 990, which implies that a + 3c = 10
  Since a, b, c are digits, we have 0 <= a, b, c <= 9. 
  Therefore, 0 <= a + 3c <= 9 + 3*9 = 36.
  Hence, a+3c = 10 implies that a=1, c=3.
  Then, 
  M = 100a + 10b + c = 100*1 + 10b + 3 = 103 + 10b
  For M to be greater than 300, we need 103 + 10b > 300, which implies that b > 19/10
  Since b is a digit, we have b >= 2.
  Therefore, there are 8 choices for b (namely, b = 2, 3, ..., 9) that satisfy the condition.
  Hence, there are 8 values of M that are more than 300.

Topic: Math
Question: Everyone in the family earns money each month. If the total income of a family per month is $9000 and the median income is $3000, how many members are there in the family?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 3
  C: 4
  D: 5
  E: 6
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - Median is the middle value of a dataset.
  - The total income divided by the number of members gives the average income per member.
  - If the median is $3000, then there are members earning more than $3000 and members earning less than $3000.

Calculation:
  - Let's assume there are n members in the family.
  - The median value is the income earned by the (n+1)/2-th member.
  - Median = $3000
  - Total Income = $9000
  - Total Income / n = Average Income per Member
  - Average Income per Member cannot be less than Median Income.
  - Therefore, Average Income per Member = Median Income = $3000
  - $9000 / n = $3000
  - n = 3

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Median income is the value separating the higher half from the lower half of the incomes in a distribution.

Calculation:
  If the median is $3000, then there are individuals whose monthly income is greater than $3000 and those who earn less than $3000.
  Let "n" be the number of family members.
  If we order their incomes increasingly, then the three middle values must be equal to the median. Since the median is 3000, then 3000 is the income of the second and third earners.
  The total monthly income of the family is $9000, which means that the sum of the incomes of the three middle earners is $3000 x 3 = $9000.
  Therefore, $9000 is earned by three individuals, so there are three members in the family.

Action: Answer("B")

  The total monthly income of the family is $9000.

Response 8:
Knowledge: 
  Median income is the middle income of a data set when it is arranged in order from lowest to highest.
  The total income of a family per month is the sum of all the individual incomes.
  If we know the median income and the total income, we can figure out how many members there are in the family. 

Let's suppose there are "n" family members.

If "n" is odd, then the median income is earned by the middle person in the order of incomes.
If "n" is even, then the median income is the average of the two incomes in the middle of the order.

So, in this case, the median income is $3000, which means that it is either the income of the 3rd person (if "n" is odd) or the average of the incomes of the 3rd and 4th persons (if "n" is even).

In both cases, we can assume that all other members of the family earn the same income, which is equal to (total income - median income)/(n-1).

Action: Answer("C") 

We have: 
total income = $9000
median income = $3000

If we assume that there are 4 family members, then the 3rd and 4th members each earn $3000, and the other two members each earn ($9000-$3000)/(4-1) = $2000.

The total income of the family is then: 
2 x $2000 + 2 x $3000 = $4000 + $6000 = $10000

This is too high, so we need to try with a smaller number of family members.

If we assume that there are 3 family members, then the 2nd member earns $3000, and the other two members each earn ($9000-$3000)/(3-1) = $3000.

The total income of the family is then: 
2 x $3000 + $3000 = $6000 + $3000 = $9000

This matches the given total income of the family, so we have found the correct answer. Hence, the number of family members is  C: 4.
Response 9:
Knowledge: 
  * Median is the middle value in a sorted list of numbers. Half the numbers are bigger than the median and half are smaller.
  * The median income of $3000 indicates that at least half of the family members earn $3000 or more per month.
  * If we divide the total monthly income by the number of family members, we can find the average income per person in the family.
Action: 
  * Let's assume there are 'n' members in the family.
  * Since the median income is $3000, there must be at least 'n/2' members earning $3000 or more per month.
  * Let's assume 'm' members earn exactly $3000 per month. Then there must be 'n/2 - m' members who earn less than $3000 per month.
  * Then, the total income of the family is: $3000m + (n/2 - m)x<$3000.
  * We know the total income is $9000, so we can solve for 'm' and 'n': 
  		$3000m + (n/2 - m)x<$3000 = $9000.
		->  $1500m + (n/2 - m)x<$3000.
		->  $1500m + $3000<$3000.
		->  $1500m<$0.
  * Since $1500m cannot be less than $0, it means that there are no family members earning exactly $3000 per month. So, all the 'n' family members earn more than $3000 per month.
  * Let's assume 'a' is the number of additional members (aside from 'n/2') who earn more than $3000 per month. Then we have: 
  		$n/2 + a = n  ->  a = n/2.
  * Therefore, the total income of the family can be written as: 
  		$9000 = ($3000 x n/2) + ($3000 x n/2 + $3000 x n/2).
  		$9000 = $3000 x n.
		-> n = 3
  * There are 3 members in the family.

Question: A starts a business with Rs.40,000. After 2 months, B joined him with Rs.60,000. C joined them after some more time with Rs.120,000. At the end of the year, out of a total profit of Rs.375,000, C gets Rs.150,000 as his share. How many months after B joined the business, did C join?
Choices:
  A: 2 months
  B: 4 months
  C: 23 months
  D: 24 months
  E: 84 months
Response 0:
Let the number of months from the start of the business until C joined be x, and let the total number of months be 12. 

After 2 months, A's contribution to the business = Rs.40000*2 = Rs.80000.
Similarly, B's contribution after he joined is (12-2)=10 months, so it is Rs.60000*10 = Rs.600000.
C's contribution after he joined is (12-x) months, so it is Rs.120000*(12-x).
Total profit = Rs.375000. 
If C gets Rs.150,000 as his share, then the sum of the others' share = Rs.375,000 - Rs.150,000 = Rs.225,000.
A and B's share is Rs.80000 + Rs.600000 = Rs.680,000. 
So we have:
Rs.680,000 + Rs.120000*(12-x) = Rs.225,000 + Rs.150,000
Rs.800,000 - Rs.225,000 = Rs.120,000x - Rs.150,000
Rs.575,000 = Rs.120,000x - Rs.150,000
x = (Rs.575,000 + Rs.150,000) / Rs.120,000
x = 5.75

Therefore, C joined after 5.75 months, which is closest to 4 months.

  - If C gets Rs. 150,000 as his share and the total profit is Rs. 375,000, then the profit-sharing ratio is (x:y:z) = (???:???:120,000)

  Total investment = (40,000 x 12) + (60,000 x 10) + (120,000 x (2 months - x))
                   = 480,000 + 600,000 + (240,000 - 120,000x)
                   = 1,320,000 - 120,000x
  As C gets Rs. 150,000 as his share, the profit-sharing ratio is (x:y:120,000) = (1320000-120000x) : 600000 : 120000

  (1320000-120000x) : 600000 : 120000 = (???????:???????:120000)

A : B : C = 8 : 10 : 2x

A : B : C = 8 : 10 : 2x

Percentage of C's share of profit = 40%

2x/18+2x = 40/100
2x/18+2x = 2/5
10x = 36 + 4x
6x = 36
x = 6

Question: [(272 - 32) (124 + 176)] / (17 x 15 - 15) = ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 2.25
  C: 300
  D: 400
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  We should follow the PEMDAS rule which stands for Parentheses, Exponents, Multiplication and Division, and Addition and Subtraction, and solve the expression from left to right. 
  First, inside the parentheses, 272 - 32 = 240 and 124 + 176 = 300.
  [(272 - 32) (124 + 176)] / (17 x 15 - 15) = [240 x 300] / (255) = 72000 / 255 = 282.35...
Knowledge:
  None of the answer choices match the calculated value. So, the answer is None of these.
Action: Answer("E")

Knowledge:
  [(a - b) (c + d)] = ac + ad - bc - bd
Action: Answer("C")  

[(272 - 32) (124 + 176)] / (17 x 15 - 15) = [(240) (300)] / (255) 
                                      = (72,000) / (255) 
                                      = 282.35294118...

Rounded to the nearest whole number, the answer is 300.
Response 2:

  To solve this expression, we need to follow the order of operations (also known as PEMDAS). 
  1. First, we calculate the expression inside the parentheses: (272 - 32) = 240 and (124 + 176) = 300.
  2. Then, we multiply these two numbers: 240 x 300 = 72000.
  3. Next, we calculate the expression inside the second set of parentheses: 17 x 15 = 255.
  4. We subtract 15 from 255: 255 - 15 = 240.
  5. Finally, we divide the result from step 2 by the result from step 4: 72000 / 240 = 300.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 59 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A certain liquid passes through a drain at a rate of w/25 gallons every x seconds. At that rate, how many minutes will it take y gallons to pass through the drain?
Choices:
  A: y/(1200xy)
  B: 20xy/w
  C: 5xy/(12w)
  D: w/(3xy)
  E: 3y/(wx)
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - To solve the problem, we need to find the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain.
  - The rate at which the liquid passes through the drain is w/25 gallons every x seconds.
  - We can use the formula: time = volume/rate
  - We need to convert the time to minutes by dividing by 60.
  
Solution:
  - Rate = w/25 gallons every x seconds
  - Rate = w/25*60 gallons every x/60 minutes
  - Rate = w/1500 gallons every x/60 minutes
  - Time = y/(w/1500 * x/60) minutes
  - Time = y * 60 * 1500 / (w * x) minutes
  - Time = 5xy/ (wx)
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  The formula for finding the time it takes to pass through a drain at a constant rate is Time = Amount/Rate.
  Amount of liquid that passes through the drain in t seconds = rt, where r is the rate of the liquid per second.
  To convert seconds to minutes, we need to divide by 60.
  
Solution:
  If the rate of the liquid is w/25 gallons every x seconds, then the rate of the liquid per second is (w/25)/x gallons.
  The amount of liquid that passes through the drain in t seconds is rt = [(w/25)/x]t = wt/(25x) gallons.
  To find how many minutes it will take y gallons to pass through the drain, we can set the amount to y gallons and solve for t in minutes:
  y = wt/(25x)
  t = (25xy)/w
  t (in minutes) = (25xy)/(60w)
  t (in minutes) = (5xy)/(12w)
  
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  - To solve this problem, we can use the formula: time = amount of liquid / rate of flow.
  - The rate of flow is w/25 gallons every x seconds.
  - To convert seconds to minutes, we divide by 60.
  
Solution:
  - The total time in minutes that it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain can be calculated as:
    time = amount of liquid / rate of flow
         = y gallons / (w/25 gallons per x seconds)
         = y gallons * (25 gallons per x seconds) / w
         = (25xy / w) * (y / 25xy) * (60 / 1)
         = 60y / wx
  - Therefore, the answer is (E) 3y/(wx).

  Simplifying:
  1 / (25x/w*y) = 1/y

  Time is measured in minutes instead of seconds so we need to convert the rate from gallons/sec to gallons/min.

  Substituting the values we get T = y/(12w/x) = xy/(12w) minutes.
  Therefore, the answer is (C) 5xy/(12w).
Response 7:
Knowledge: 
  - The rate at which the liquid passes through the drain is w/25 gallons per x seconds.
  - We want to find out how many minutes it will take for y gallons to pass through the drain.
  - There are 60 seconds in a minute.
  
Solution:
  - The rate at which the liquid passes through the drain is w/25 gallons per x seconds.
  - To find out how long it will take for y gallons to pass through the drain, we need to multiply the rate by the time.
  - Let z be the time it takes for y gallons to pass through the drain in minutes.
  - We know that the rate is w/25 gallons per x seconds, which is equivalent to (w/25)*60/x gallons per minute (converting seconds to minutes).
  - Therefore, we can write the equation (w/25)*60/x * z = y.
  - Solving for z: z = y * (25*x)/(60*w)
  - Simplifying: z = y * 5*x/(12*w)
  - Therefore, the answer is (C) 5xy/(12w).

Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth?
Choices:
  A: 56
  B: 58
  C: 60
  D: 62
  E: 64
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  If the area of a triangle is given by A = (1/2)bh, then the base b and the height h of the triangle can be calculated using A = (1/2)bh or b = 2A/h or h = 2A/b.
  The area of a rectangle is given by A = lw, where l is the length and w is the width of the rectangle.
  The perimeter of a rectangle is given by P = 2l + 2w.
  A square is a special case of a rectangle.
  
Solution:
  Let x be the length of the side of the original square piece of cloth, then its area is A1 = x^2 square feet.
  After trimming, the rectangular piece has one side with length x-4 feet and the other side with length x feet. Its area is A2 = (x-4)x = x^2 - 4x square feet.
  The two triangles are congruent and have equal areas of 70 square feet each. 
  Let b be the base of a triangle, then the height of the triangle is h = 2(70)/b = 140/b feet.
  By the Pythagorean theorem, we have b^2 + h^2 = x^2, so
  b^2 + (140/b)^2 = x^2
  b^4 - x^2b^2 + 140^2 = 0
  b^2 = (x^2 ± sqrt(x^4 - 4*140^2))/2
  We take the positive root because b is a length.
  b^2 = (x^2 + sqrt(x^4 - 4*140^2))/2
  b = sqrt(x^2 + sqrt(x^4 - 4*140^2))/sqrt(2)
  The perimeter of the rectangle is P = 2(x-4) + 2x = 4x - 8 feet
  The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x feet.
  We can solve for x as follows:
  A1 - A2 = 2 * 70 = 140
  x^2 - (x^2 - 4x) = 140
  4x = 140
  x = 35
  Therefore, the perimeter of the original square piece of cloth is 4x = 140 feet.
  The answer is (None of the Above).
  
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

So x^2/2 - 2x^2/25 = 70.
Solving this by quadratic equation, we get x = 25 or -10/3. The negative solution is extraneous, so x = 25.

The original square had a perimeter of 4x = 100 feet.

Area = (Base * Height) / 2

70 = (Base * Height) / 2
140 = Base * Height

Length = sqrt(Height^2 + Base^2)
Length = sqrt(2*Base^2)
Length = Base * sqrt(2)
Finally, we can use the dimensions of the rectangle to find the perimeter of the original square cloth (before being trimmed).

2x^2 - 8x - 16 = 0
x^2 - 4x - 8 = 0

x = (4 ± 2*sqrt(3))
Since x represents the length of one side of the original square cloth, the perimeter is:

  x^2 + x^2 - 8x + 16 = 392
  2x^2 - 8x - 376 = 0
  x^2 - 4x - 188 = 0
  Solving this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula, we get:
  x = 14 + 6*sqrt(3) feet (ignoring the negative root)
  The perimeter of the original square piece of cloth was 4x = 56 + 24*sqrt(3) feet.

Question: A rectangular parking space is marked out by painting three of its sides. If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, and the sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, then what is the area of the parking space in square feet?
Choices:
  A: 46
  B: 81
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The area of a rectangle can be calculated as A = lw, where l is the length of the rectangle and w is its width.
  Three sides of the rectangle are painted, so the unpainted side is the width w.
  The sum of the lengths of the painted sides is 37 feet, which equals 2l + w. 

Action: 
  We know that w = 9 feet, so:
  2l + w = 2l + 9 = 37
  Solving for l, we get: l = 14
  
  Therefore, the area of the parking space is A = lw = (14)(9) = 126 square feet.
  
Answer: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The area of a rectangle is the product of its length and width.
  If the length of the unpainted side is 9 feet, then this side corresponds to the width of the rectangle.
  Let's call the length of the painted side that is adjacent to the unpainted side "x", and the length of the other painted side "y". Then, we know that x + y + 9 = 37.
  We can simplify this to x + y = 28.
  We also know that the area of the rectangle is x * 9, since the unpainted side has length 9 feet.
Action: 
  We have two equations:
  x + y = 28
  x + 9 = 37 - y
  We can solve for x in the second equation:
  x = 28 - y
  Substitute that into the second equation:
  28 - y + 9 = 37 - y
  37 - y - y = 37 - 9
  y = 14
  Then, x = 28 - y = 14
  The area of the parking space is x * 9 = 14 * 9 = 126 square feet.
  Answer("C")

    2(length + 9) = l1 + l2 + 2w = 28 + 2(9) = 46

  Finally, we can compute the area:
    A = length * width = 14 * 9 = 126

Topic: Math
Question: Hoses A and B spout water at different constant rates, and hose A can fill a certain pool in 8 hours. Hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours and the two hoses, working together, then finished filling the pool in another 3 hours. How many hours would it have taken hose B, working alone, to fill the entire pool?
Choices:
  A: 8
  B: 15
  C: 12
  D: 6
  E: 3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If we want to fill a pool with volume V, and hose A can fill it in tA hours, then the rate of hose A is V/tA. 
  If hose A and hose B together can fill the pool in tAB hours, then the total volume that the two hoses can handle together in one hour is V/tAB.
  From the problem, we know hose A filled the pool alone for the first 2 hours, so it filled 2V/8 of the pool on its own.
  We also know that Hose A and Hose B, working together, finished filling the pool in another 3 hours so that they filled 3V/8 of the pool together.
  We can use these facts to form two equations:
    (1) 2V/8 = (V/8) * 2 = rate of hose A * 2
    (2) 3V/8 = (V/8) * 3 = (rate of hose A + rate of hose B) * 3

Action: 
We want to find the number of hours it would take for hose B to fill the pool alone, so we need to solve for the rate of hose B first and then use it to find the number of hours. 

Let x be the time (in hours) it would take hose B to fill the pool alone.
The rate of hose B is therefore V/tB = V/x.

From equation (1), we can find the rate of hose A:
  2V/8 = rate of hose A * 2
  rate of hose A = V/8

From equation (2), we can find the total rate of hose A and hose B together:
  3V/8 = (rate of hose A + rate of hose B) * 3
  1/8 + V/x = 3/8
  V/x = 2/8 = 1/4

Now we can solve for x:
  V/x = 1/4
  x = 4

Answer: Answer("D")

Let's assume the two numbers are 3x and 5x.
Also, (3x-9)/(5x-9) = 12/23, since we are told that if we subtract 9 from each, the new ratio is 12:23.

  12(5x-9) = 23(3x-9)
  60x - 108 = 69x - 207
  9x = 99
  x = 11

Therefore, the smaller number is 3x = 3(11) = 33.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 65 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then what is the value of m?
Choices:
  A: -23.5
  B: -17.5
  C: -10.5
  D: -16.2
  E: Cannot be determined
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If a quadratic equation is given as ax^2 + bx + c = 0, then the sum of roots is -b/a and the product of roots is c/a.
  
Let the other root be p. Therefore, using the sum of roots formula, we have p + 1.5 = -m. Using the product of roots formula, we have p(1.5) = 22.
So we have two equations:
p + 1.5 = -m    ...(1)
p(1.5) = 22     ...(2)

We can solve these equations simultaneously to get the value of m.

From equation (2), we get p = 22/1.5 = 14.67
Substitute p value in equation (1), we get  14.67 + 1.5 = -m
Therefore, m = -16.17

Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0 is given by -b/a, and the product of the roots is given by c/a.
  If one of the roots of a quadratic equation is given, then the sum and product of the roots can be found, and from there we can find the value of the unknown coefficient.

Solution: 
  Let's denote the second root of the equation as r.
  We know that the product of the roots is 22, so:
  1.5r = 22/r
  1.5r^2 = 22
  r^2 = 22/1.5
  r^2 = 14.67
  The sum of the roots is -m, so:
  1.5 + r = -m
  r = -m - 1.5
  Substituting the value of r found above:
  -m - 1.5 = sqrt(14.67) OR -m - 1.5 = -sqrt(14.67)
  Solving the first equation for m:
  -m = sqrt(14.67) + 1.5
  m = -sqrt(14.67) - 1.5
  Solving the second equation for m:
  -m = -sqrt(14.67) + 1.5
  m = sqrt(14.67) - 1.5
  Since the possible values of m are both negative, our answer is:
Action: Answer("D")  
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  If one of the roots of a quadratic equation is known, we can use Vieta's formulas to find the coefficients of the equation. 
  Vieta's formulas state:
    - For a quadratic equation ax^2 + bx + c = 0, the sum of the roots is -b/a and the product of the roots is c/a.
  If one root of x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5, then the other root can be found by using the fact that the product of the roots is 22. 

Calculation:
  If one root is 1.5, then the other root must be 22/1.5 = 14.67 (approx).
  Applying Vieta's formulas:
    - Sum of roots = -m/1 = -m
    - Product of roots = 1.5 * 14.67 = 22
  Therefore, -m = 22 + 1.5 * 14.67 = 43.5 (approx)
  Hence, m = -43.5

Response 3:
Knowledge:
  A quadratic equation of the form ax^2 + bx + c = 0 has two roots, given by (-b ± sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)) / 2a.
  
To solve the problem, we need to use the fact that one of the roots of the quadratic equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 is 1.5. This means that we can write:

(x - 1.5)(x + r) = 0

where r is the other root.

Expanding the left-hand side, we get:

x^2 + (r - 1.5)x - 1.5r = 0

Comparing coefficients with the original equation x^2 + mx + 22 = 0, we get:

r - 1.5 = m
-1.5r = 22

Multiplying the first equation by -1.5 and adding to the second equation, we get:

(-1.5)(r - 1.5) - 1.5r = -m + 22
-3r + 3 = -m + 22
-m = -3r + 19

Now we can substitute the second equation into the last equation to get:

-m = -3(22/-1.5) + 19
-m = -44/3 + 57/3
-m = 13/3

Therefore, the value of m is 13/3.

  The sum of the roots is 1.5 + (-14.67) = -13.17.
Action: Answer("A") 
  (m is the negation of the sum of the roots, so m = -(-13.17) = 13.17, which is closest to -23.5)

The quadratic formula is: x = (-b ± sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)) / 2a
The sum of the roots of a quadratic equation is -b/a, where b and a are the coefficients of x and x^2 respectively.

  If r is one of the roots of a quadratic equation ax^2 + bx + c = 0, then (x - r) is one of its factors.
  We are given one of the roots of the quadratic equation, that is, x = 1.5 and c = 22.
  Therefore, we can determine the value of m by using the formula for sum of roots: sum of roots = -b/a = -m/a.
  
Calculation:
  Using formula, sum of roots = -b/a = -m/a.
  Let's find the other root of the quadratic equation using (x - r) factor: (x - r)(x - s) = 0, where s is the other root.
  We know that r = 1.5 and c = 22. Therefore, (x - 1.5)(x - s) = 0,  which expands to x^2 - (s+1.5)x + 1.5s = 0.
  Since the above quadratic equation is equivalent to x^2 + mx + 22 = 0, we can equate their coefficients to determine m and s.
  By comparing the coefficients, we have:
      -s - 1.5 = m
      1.5s = 22
  Solving the second equation for s, we get s = 22/1.5 = 14.6666....
  Substituting s in the first equation yields, m = -s - 1.5 = -14.6666... - 1.5 = -16.1666....
  Rounding to one decimal place gives, m = -16.2

Topic: Math
Question: In a large forest, 300 deer were caught, tagged, and returned during 2001. During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, of which only 20 had tags from the previous year. If the percent of deer in the forest that had tags during the second year and were caught in the 500 deer sample is representative of the percent of the total deer population in the forest with tags, what is the total deer population in the forest (assuming no change in population between 2001 and 2002)?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 500
  C: 5000
  D: 6000
  E: 7500
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let D1 be the total deer population in the year 2001. 
  Let D2 be the total deer population in the year 2002. 
  During 2001, 300 deer were tagged, and assumed were randomly released back to the forest.
  During 2002, 500 deer were caught at random, and the proportion of deer with tags was 20/500.
  The proportion of deer with tags in the total population of 2002 is assumed to be the same as the proportion of tagged deer caught in the sample of 500 deer.
Action: 
  Let's find out the number of tags at the end of the 2002 hunting season: 300 tagged from 2001 + 20 tagged from 2002 = 320 tags.
  If 20 out of 500 deer were tagged, then the proportion of tagged deer in the sample is 20/500 = 0.04.
  Assuming that the proportion of tagged deer in the population is the same as in the sample, we can set up an equation:
    320 / D2 = 0.04
  Solving for D2, we get:
    D2 = 320 / 0.04
    D2 = 8000
  Therefore, Answer is E: 7500
Response 1:
Let us first consider the number of tagged deer in 2002. We know that 20 deer that were caught had tags from the previous year, and we are assuming that this is representative of the total population of deer with tags. Therefore, we can set up a proportion:

20 tagged deer / 500 caught = x tagged deer / total population

Solving for x, we get:

x = (20 / 500) * total population
x = 0.04 * total population

Now, we know that 300 deer were tagged in 2001, so the total number of deer that were tagged over the two-year period is 300 + x. Substituting x in, we get:

300 + 0.04 * total population

But we also know that the total number of deer caught in 2002 is 500, so we can set up another proportion:

300 + 0.04 * total population = 500 caught

Solving for total population, we get:

total population = (500 - 300) / 0.04
total population = 5,000

Therefore, the total deer population in the forest is 5,000.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 68 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: On dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder. The sum of the digits of N is:
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 11
  C: 12
  D: 13
  E: 14
Response 0:
Let's say the remainder is x when 2272 and 875 are divided by N. 
From this, we can form the following equations: 
2272 ≡ x (mod N)
875 ≡ x (mod N)

We can find the value of N by finding the GCD of the differences between the two numbers and the remainder: 

GCD(2272 - x, 875 - x) = N

We want N to be a 3-digit number, so we can first look for factors of the GCD that are 3-digit numbers. 

Factors of GCD(2272 - x, 875 - x): 
1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 8, 11, 16, 22, 24, 33, 44, 48, 55, 88, 132, 176, 264, 440, 660, 1100

The only 3-digit factor of the GCD is 11. Therefore, we can say: 

GCD(2272 - x, 875 - x) = 11

From this, we can form the following equations: 
2272 ≡ x (mod 11)
875 ≡ x (mod 11)

We can simplify these equations by adding up the digits of each number: 
2 + 2 + 7 + 2 = 13, which is equivalent to 2 (mod 11)
8 + 7 + 5 = 20, which is equivalent to 9 (mod 11)

So, we have: 
x ≡ 2 (mod 11)
x ≡ 9 (mod 11)

The only solution to these congruences is x ≡ 2 (mod 11). 

Now, we need to find a 3-digit number N such that: 
2272 ≡ 2 (mod N)
875 ≡ 2 (mod N)

We can use the same method as before to find the GCD of 2270 and 873. 

GCD(2270, 873) = 19

The factors of 19 are 1 and 19, which are both 2-digit numbers. Therefore, N cannot be 19. 

We need to increase N by a multiple of 19 so that it becomes a 3-digit number. Since N must be less than both 2270 and 873, the only multiple of 19 that works is 38. 

Therefore, N = 19 * 38 = 722. 

The sum of the digits of N is 7 + 2 + 2 = 11.

Action: Answer("E")  
The sum of digits of N is 20 for the value of N=1397.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
In order to find the remainder obtained when a number is divided by another number, we can take the difference between the dividend and divisor when the dividend is divided by the divisor. That is, if a and b are both integers and b is not zero, then the remainder when a is divided by b is equal to a - b * floor(a/b), where floor(a/b) is the quotient when a is divided by b rounded down to the nearest integer.

We know that: 
1) Remainder when 2272 is divided by N = Remainder when 875 is divided by N 
2) Remainder when 2272 is divided by N can be calculated as 2272 - N * floor(2272/N)
3) Remainder when 875 is divided by N can be calculated as 875 - N * floor(875/N)

Thus, we get two equations:
2272 - N * floor(2272/N) = 875 - N * floor(875/N)
(N * floor(2272/N)) - (N * floor(875/N)) = 1397

1397 can be expressed as (N * a) - (N * b), where a and b are integers. This can be factored as N * (a - b) = 1397
Since N is a 3-digit number, we can assume that (a - b) is less than 1000.

After some calculations, the factors of 1397 are (1, 1397) and (17, 82). Since N is a 3-digit number, the only possible pair is (17, 82). So, a - b = 82 - 17 = 65.

We are asked to find the sum of the digits of N. Since N is a 3-digit number, it can be expressed as 100x + 10y + z (where x, y, and z are digits of N). Therefore, we have:
N = 100x + 10y + z
N = (100 + 10 + 1)(x + y + z) - 11y - 99x
N = 111(x + y + z) - 11y - 99x
N = 11(9x - y) + 111z

So, the sum of the digits of N is the sum of the digits of 9x - y + z. Since N is a 3-digit number, we know that 9x - y + z must be between 100 and 999.

    875 = p2 * N + r1   (where p2 is the quotient)
To find the sum of the digits of N, we need to calculate the value of N.
We can find the value of N by taking the LCM of (2272-r1) and (875-r1), which is equal to LCM(p1, p2)*N. 

Solution:
Given, on dividing 2272 and 875 by a 3-digit number N, we get the same remainder.
Let's assume the 3-digit number N be 'xyz'. Then, 
2272 = p1 * N + r1    ---(1)
875 = p2 * N + r1    ---(2)
where 'r1' is the common remainder obtained on dividing 2272 and 875 by N, and p1 and p2 are the quotients respectively.

Subtracting equation (2) from (1), we get
1397 = (p1 - p2) * N

Given, N is a 3-digit number. So, the value of N should be a factor of 1397.
1397 is a prime number and factors of prime numbers are 1 and the number itself. Therefore, the value of (p1 - p2) can only be 1.

So, 1397 = N
=> N = 1397

Sum of the digits of N = 1+3+9+7 = 20
Action: Answer("None of the Above")  (The given answer options do not have the option for 20, which is the correct answer)
Response 9:
Knowledge: 
  If we divide a number x by a number y and get the same remainder r for both, then the difference between x and y must be a multiple of the common remainder r.
  For example, if:
     x = 10, y = 3, and r = 1, then 10/3 = 3 with a remainder of 1, and 7/3 = 2 with a remainder of 1. Here, the difference between x and y is 7, which is a multiple of the remainder 1.
  We are given that 2272 and 875 leave the same remainder when divided by N. This means that the difference between 2272 and 875 (which is 1397) must be a multiple of N.
  To find the sum of the digits of N, we need to find N itself.
  We know that N divides 1397, so we can find all factors of 1397 and check which ones are 3-digit numbers.
  Prime factorizing 1397, we get: 1397 = 19 * 73
  The factors of 1397 are: 1, 19, 73, and 1397.
  Out of these, only 73 is a 2-digit number. Therefore, N = 73, and the sum of its digits is 7+3 = 10.

  E: 20

  Now, we can use the formula time = work / rate to get the time it takes Jill to finish the remaining work:
  Time taken by Jill = Work done by Jill / Rate of Jill
  Work done by Jill = One-third of the total work (since Jack has done two-thirds of the work)
  Work done by Jill = (1/3) * (3/2) = 1/2
  Therefore, Time taken by Jill = (1/2) / (1/240) 
  Time taken by Jill = 120 hours

Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Let x be the time taken for Mr.Sam to travel to the city by car (in hours).
Round trip by train takes 17 hours (to go by train and return by car) and this is 4 hours more than the time taken for both trips to take place by train. This means the time it takes to go by train is (17-4)/2 = 6.5 hours.
We know that the total time taken by car for the round trip would be 2x hours.
Therefore, we can write the equation:
2x = (x + 6.5) + (x + 6.5)
Simplifying this equation, we get:
2x = 2x + 13
0 = 13
We obtain a contradiction which implies that the answer is None of the Above. 
However, the most likely answer is that there is an error in the problem since the question doesn't make sense. Therefore, the best action is to Answer("None of the Above").
Response 1:
Knowledge:

  Then, he takes 17 -x hours to travel back by train.
  So, the total time taken = x + (17-x) = 17.
  When he travels both ways by train, then the time taken = 2 * 17 -4 = 30 hours (he loses 4 hours).
  Therefore, the time taken if he had traveled by car in both ways = (30 - 2x) hours
  
Calculation:
  (30-2x) = x + (17-x)
  30-2x = 17
  2x = 13
  x = (13/2) = 6.5

Let's assume that Mr. Sam takes X hours to reach the city by car and Y hours to return, when he travels both ways by car.
Using the above information, we can create the following equation: 

    X + Y = 17        (by train to a certain city and return by car)
    X - 4 + Y - 4 = X + Y      (loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train)

Response 3:
Let's denote the time it takes Mr.Sam to go to the city by train as `t1`. Similarly, we will denote the time it takes him to go back by car as `t2`. 
From the question, we know that `t1 + t2 = 17` and `2t1 - 4 = t2`. 
We can use the second equation to substitute `t2` in the first equation and solve for `t1`: 
```
2t1 - 4 + t1 = 17
3t1 = 21
t1 = 7
``` 
Now we can use `t1` to solve for `t2`: 
```
2t1 - 4 = t2
2(7) - 4 = t2
t2 = 10
``` 
Finally, we know that Mr.Sam spent `t1 + t2 = 7 + 10 = 17` hours traveling. Therefore, if he had traveled both ways by car, he would have taken `2t2 = 2(10) = 20` hours.

Equation 2: x + y = n, where n is the total number of coins.

20x + 25(n-x) = 340
Simplifying the equation, we get:
5x = 340 - 25n
Dividing both sides by 5, we get:
x = 68 - 5n

Since x has to be a non-negative integer, the minimum value of x occurs when 68 - 5n is 0 or positive and divisible by 5.
The largest multiple of 5 that is less than or equal to 68 is 65, which gives n = 3. Plugging n = 3 into the equation x = 68 - 5n, we get x = 3.

Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins is 3.

Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997

1. a + b + c = 17
2. a^2 + b^2 + c^2= 109
3. 100a + 10b +c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a

Simplifying equation 3, we get:
99a - 99c = 495
a - c = 5

We can substitute the value of a - c in equation 1 to get:
2b + 5 = 17
b = 6

x + y + z = 17     (1)
x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 109      (2)

x = z + 5

x^2 + 36 = 109
x^2 = 73
The only one-digit integer which when squared gives a two-digit number starting with 7 is 8. Thus, x = 8. Therefore, the number we seek is 100x + 10y + z = 806.

We verify that 806 - 495 = 311, which is indeed 100z + 10y + x with the digits written in reversed order.

Question: Fernando purchased a university meal plan that allows him to have a total of 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week. If the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights, how many options does he have to allocate his meals?
Choices:
  A: 5C3*4C3
  B: 5C4*4C2
  C: 5C2*4C4
  D: 5C6*4C5
  E: 4C3*4C3
Response 0:

  Fernando has 3 options for which lunch to eat during weekdays.
  Fernando has 2 options for which dinner to eat during weekdays.
  Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday night.
  A: 5C3*4C3 would give us the number of ways to choose 3 out of 5 weekdays for lunches and 3 out of 4 weekdays for dinners, but this would not account for the fact that Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday night.
  B: 5C4*4C2 would give us the number of ways to choose 4 out of 5 weekdays for lunches and 2 out of 4 weekdays for dinners. However, this would not account for the fact that Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday night.
  C: 5C2*4C4 would give us the number of ways to choose 2 out of 5 weekdays for lunches and 4 out of 4 weekdays for dinners. This does not account for the fact that Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday night.
  D: 5C6*4C5 would give us the number of ways to choose 6 out of 5 weekdays for lunches and 5 out of 4 weekdays for dinners, which is not possible.
  E: 4C3*4C3 would give us the number of ways to choose 3 out of 4 weekdays for lunches and 3 out of 4 weekdays for dinners, but this would not account for the fact that Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday night.
Action: Answer("B") 
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Fernando has 3 options for lunches and 2 options for dinner (excluding Friday dinner).
  Fernando's Friday dinner is always at home.
  A combination can be calculated by using the combination formula: nCr = n! / r!(n - r)! where n is the total number of options and r is the number of options we are choosing.
  
Calculation:
  Fernando needs to choose 3 lunches out of 3 options (combinations 3C3) and 2 dinners out of 2 options (combinations 2C2).
  The remaining dinner is on a day other than Friday, so Fernando can choose from the 5 remaining days in the week (combinations 5C1).
  Therefore, the total number of options is 3C3 * 2C2 * 5C1 = 1 * 1 * 5 = 5.

Fernando has 2 options for dinners: he can either eat at the cafeteria on a weekday or go home on Friday night.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 74 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  - The volume of a cube with edge length "a" is given by Vc = a^3
  - The volume of a sphere with radius "r" is given by Vs = (4/3)πr^3
  - The diameter of the sphere is equal to the edge length of the cube
  - The radius of the sphere is half of the diameter

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 75 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: There are ten lime soda bottles on a table in a restaurant. They are to be served among two different groups of customers consisting of 5 members each. How many ways are there to create these 2 groups?
Choices:
  A: 90
  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525
Response 0:
Knowledge: The number of ways to form r groups from n distinct objects without regard to order is given by the combination formula C(n,r) which is n! / (r! * (n-r)!).
  
There are 10 lime soda bottles. We want to divide them into two groups of five customers each. We can first select the first group of customers in C(10,5) ways. Then, we can select the second group of customers in C(5,5) ways. However, since we are counting the same division twice (the order of selecting the groups doesn't matter), we need to divide by 2. Hence, the total number of ways to create these two groups is C(10,5) * C(5,5) / 2.

Computation: 
  C(10,5) = 252
  C(5,5) = 1
  Total number of ways = 252 * 1 / 2 = 126

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  This is a combinatorics problem since we want to know the number of ways to create groups.
  The formula for finding the number of ways to select r items from n items (nCr) is n!/((r!)(n-r)!).
  In this problem, we have 10 lime soda bottles and want to divide them into groups of 5.
  We can use the formula for combinations, nCr = n!/(r!(n-r)!), to calculate the number of ways to divide the soda bottles into groups of 5.

Action: Answer("252")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  This problem can be solved using combination formula.
  Combination formula: n choose k = n! / k!(n-k)!
  where ! denotes factorial, n is the total number of items, and k is the number of items being selected.
  
Solution:
  Total number of ways to select 5 bottles from 10 bottles is given by 10 choose 5.
  10 choose 5 = 10!/(5!(10-5)!) = 252
  This is the number of ways to create the first group.
  Once the first group is selected, the remaining bottles form the second group.
  Therefore, the answer is 252. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Knowledge: This is a combinations problem. The formula to find the number of combinations of n objects taken r at a time is C(n,r) = n! / (r! * (n-r)!).
Action: Answer("C")

There are C(10, 5) ways to choose the first group, and once we've chosen those 5 bottles, the remaining 5 bottles will go to the second group. Therefore, the total number of ways to divide the bottles is C(10, 5) = 252 / (5! * 5!) = 252 / 120 = 126.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Let's start by using a Venn diagram to visualize the problem. 

[Diagram not possible in text format].

From the given information, we know that:
- The number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm. Let's call the number of files infected only by a worm "w" and the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm "x". Therefore, we have the equation: w = 2.5x.
- All 250 files fall under one of the three categories: only virus, only worm, or both virus and worm. Therefore, we have the equation: w + x + y = 250, where y is the number of files infected only by a virus.

We can use this equation to solve for y. Rearranging, we get: y = 250 - w - x.

We are given that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus. This means that y, the number of files infected only by a virus, is equal to 0.5 times the total number of files. Therefore, we have the equation: y = 0.5(250) = 125.

We can now substitute this value of y into the equation we got earlier to solve for x and w:
125 = 250 - w - x
=> w + x = 125

Also, we know that w = 2.5x. Substituting this into the above equation, we get:
2.5x + x = 125
=> 3.5x = 125
=> x = 35.71 (rounded to two decimal places)
=> w = 2.5x = 89.29
=> y = 250 - w - x = 125

Now we can use the above values to find the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm:
Number of files infected by a virus only = y = 125
Total number of files infected by a virus = y + x = 125 + 35.71 = 160.71 (rounded to two decimal places)
Total number of files infected by a worm = y + w = 125 + 89.29 = 214.29 (rounded to two decimal places)

Therefore, the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm is:
Total number of files - Total number of files infected by a worm = 250 - 214.29 = 35.71 (rounded to two decimal places)

Action: Answer("B") the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm is 70.

  (125 - b) + b = 250/2
  125 = 125
  This equation is always true, so any value of b that satisfies the first two equations will also satisfy the third equation.
  Let's try b = 40:
  w = 2.5b = 100
  v = 125 - b = 85
  The number of files that were not infected by a worm is:
  Not infected by a worm = (Total number of files) - (Files infected by a worm) = 250 - w = 150
Action: Answer("None of the Above") 
None of the given choices (A, B, C, D, E) is correct.
Response 9:
Knowledge:
  - Let V be the number of files infected by only a virus.
  - Let W be the number of files infected by only a worm.
  - Let X be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  - We know that V + W + X = 250.
  - We also know that W = 2.5X.
  - We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, which means that V is half of the total number of files that are infected in some way, so V + X = 125.

Action:
  - We know that V + W + X = 250, and V + X = 125, so W = 250 - 2X - V = 250 - 2X - 125 = 125 - 2X.
  - We also know that W = 2.5X.
  - Equating the two expressions for W, we get 2.5X = 125 - 2X, which gives us 4.5X = 125, or X = 125/4.5 = 27.78 (rounded to two decimal places).
  - Since V + X = 125, we have V = 125 - X = 125 - 27.78 = 97.22 (rounded to two decimal places).
  - Therefore, the number of files that were not infected by a worm is V = 97.22, which rounded to the nearest integer is 97.

Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs. 300.

Question: The length of the ribbon was originally 30 cm. It was reduced in the ratio 5 : 3. What is its length now?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 30
  C: 6
  D: 15
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  In a ratio of a:b, the first number is called the antecedent and the second number is called the consequent.
  If a ribbon is reduced in the ratio a:b, then the new length is (b/a) times the original length.
  
  In this case, the ribbon length was reduced in the ratio 5:3. This means:
    - antecedent = 5
    - consequent = 3
    - new length = (3/5) times the original length
    
Action: Answer("18")

  - Calculate (3/5) times the original length:
    (3/5) * 30 = 18
  - The new length of the ribbon is 18 cm.
Therefore, the answer is A: 18 cm.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Let the distance between X and Y be "d". Let "t" be the time taken by both Allen and Bob to meet for the second time. 
During the first meeting, the distance traveled by Allen is equal to the distance traveled by Bob. 
Distance traveled by Allen = speed * time = 54t
Distance traveled by Bob = speed * time = 78t
Total distance traveled by both Allen and Bob during the first meeting = 54t + 78t = 132t

During the second meeting, Allen has traveled the entire distance between X and Y, while Bob has traveled an extra 48 km. Therefore,
Distance traveled by Allen = d
Distance traveled by Bob = d + 48

During the second meeting, the distance traveled by Allen is equal to the distance traveled by Bob. 
d = 54t + d + 48 - 78t
24t = d + 48
Substituting d = 24t - 48 in the equation d = distance between X and Y:
distance between X and Y = 24t - 48
We need to find the value of "d". To do this, we need to find the value of "t".

From the equation 24t = d + 48, we know that d = 24t - 48.
Total distance traveled by both Allen and Bob = distance between X and Y + distance between X and Y = 2d
Total time taken by both Allen and Bob = time taken by Allen + time taken by Bob = t + t = 2t

From the information given in the question,
2d = 54t + 78t
2d = 132t
d = 66t

Substituting d = 24t - 48 in the above equation,
66t = 24t - 48
42t = 48
t = 8/7 hours

Therefore, distance between X and Y = 24t - 48 = 24*(8/7) - 48 = 144/7 ≈ 20.57 km
Answer: Choice A: 144km.
Response 1:
Let us consider that the distance between X and Y is d km.

After meeting for the first time, Allen would have covered d/2 km, and Bob would have covered 1.5d km.

Let the time taken for both of them to meet for the second time be t hours.

So Allen's distance covered in the second round would be 54t km.

Bob's distance covered in the second round would be 78t km.

We know that Bob covered 48km more than Allen.

Therefore, 78t - 1.5d = 54t + 0.5d + 48  (time*speed = distance)

Solving the above equation, we get d = 126 km.

Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 126 km.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
We can begin this problem by using the formula distance = speed x time. Let's denote the distance from X to Y as d, and the time it takes for Allen to reach Y for the first time as t. Since Allen travels at 54 kmph and Y is d kilometers away from X,
distance Allen covers in time t = 54t
Once Allen reaches Y, the total distance remaining to X is d - 54t. At this point, Bob starts from Y and moves towards X. Bob travels at 78 kmph, so the time Bob takes to travel to the point where he meets Allen is (d - 54t) / 78.
When they meet for the first time, they have traveled a total distance of d. After this point, Allen turns back, and Bob continues moving towards X. The distance between them is now increasing at a rate of (54 + 78) = 132 kmph. They would meet for the second time when the distance between them has increased by d km.
Let's assume that the time taken for them to meet for the second time is t2. At this point, Allen has traveled a total distance of 2d, and Bob has traveled a total distance of (2d + 48) (since Bob has covered 48 km more than Allen). Using the formula distance = speed x time, we can write:
speed of Allen x time taken by Allen = 2d
54 x (2t2 - t) = 2d
speed of Bob x time taken by Bob = 2d + 48
78 x (t2 - (d - 54t)/78) = 2d + 48
Simplifying the equations, we get:
108t - 54d = 0
78t2 - 3dt + 48 = 0
We can substitute d = 108t/54 = 2t in the second equation, which gives:
39t^2 + 16t - 16 = 0
On solving, we get t = 4/3 hours. Substituting this value in d = 108t/54, we get d = 72 km.

24t2 = 48

Response 5:
Knowledge:
  The key to solving this problem is to realize that, in scenarios like this one, the ratio of time spent by both Allen and Bob traveling towards each other is the same as the ratio of their speeds.
  Let d be the distance between X and Y.
  Let t be the time it takes for Allen and Bob to meet for the first time.
  Let T be the time it takes for them to meet for the second time.
  The distance traveled by Allen before they first meet is 54t. The distance traveled by Bob is 78t.
  When they meet for the first time, the total distance they traveled is d, so 54t + 78t = d.
  After they first meet, Allen must travel an additional distance of d to get back to X. Bob must travel an additional distance of d to get back to Y. At this point, their total distance traveled is 3d, and the time they have spent traveling towards each other is T - t.
  The difference in distance traveled by Allen and Bob is then (78/132)(T - t)d - (54/132)(T - t)d = 48 km, where 78/132 and 54/132 represent the ratios of time spent by Bob and Allen, respectively.
  Simplifying this equation gives (1/11)(T - t)d = 4. Solving the first equation for t and substituting into the second equation gives (1/11)(3d/78 - d/54)d = 4.
  Solving this equation gives d = 126 km.

Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Let's assume the distance between the start and end point is D.
  Let's assume the speed during the initial (forward) journey is S1 and the speed during the return journey is S2.
  We know that D = S1*6 and D = S2*4, since the distance covered is the same in both directions.
  We also know that S2 = S1 + 12, since the speed increased by 12km/hr.
  Solving these equations simultaneously, we can find the value of D.
  To solve, we can start by substituting the expression for S2 into the second equation: D = (S1+12) * 4
  Then, substitute the first equation into this expression for D: S1*6 = (S1+12) * 4
  Simplifying this equation gives S1 = 18km/hr
  Finally, substitute this value of S1 into either of the original equations to find D: D = S1*6 = 108km
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Let the distance travelled be "d"
  Let the speed during the forward journey be "x"
  Let the speed during the return journey be "y"
  Distance = Speed * Time
  Time taken during forward journey = 6 hours
  Time taken during return journey = 4 hours
  Using the formula, speed = distance/time, we can derive the following:
  speed during the forward journey = d/6
  speed during the return journey = d/4
  The speed during the return journey is 12km/hr faster than the speed during the forward journey i.e y = x + 12

Working: 
  During the forward journey, speed = d/6
  During the return journey, speed = d/4
  We know that the speed during the return journey (d/4) is 12km/hr faster than the speed during the forward journey (d/6)
  Therefore: d/4 = d/6 + 12
  Solving the above equation, we get: d = 144km

  6s = 4s + 48
  2s = 48
  s = 24 km/h
  Using the formula d = s * t, we can calculate the distance as:
  d = 24 * 6 = 144 km

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The number of water lilies doubles every two days.
  If it takes 60 days for 1 water lily to cover the lake, that means it doubles 30 times (60/2 = 30).
  If initially, there were 64 water lilies, that means the lake has already doubled 6 times (since 2^6=64).
  We need to figure out how many more times the lake will double to be fully covered.
  We can use the formula for exponential growth: P = P0 * 2^(t/k), where P is the population at time t, P0 is the initial population, k is the doubling time, and t is the time elapsed.
  We know that P0 = 64, k = 2, and we want to find t when P = 2^30 * P0 (since the lake will be fully covered at that point).

Action: 
  P = 2^30 * P0
  t = k * log2(P/P0)
  t = 2 * log2(2^30)
  t = 60
Answer: ("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Starting from 1 water lily, the number of water lilies on the lake doubles every 2 days.
  If it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with lilies starting from 1 water lily, then on the 59th day the lake is half full of lilies. 

Calculation:
  Starting from 64 lilies, the lake is already half full of lilies.
  Therefore, the lake will be fully covered with lilies one doubling time earlier than 60 days.
  
  Doubling the water lilies: 64 * 2 = 128 (this will happen in 2 days)
  To calculate how many doubling time are needed to cover the lake:
  2^x * 64 = 2^30  (30 doubling times is 60 days)
  2^x = 2^(30-6)
  2^x = 2^24
  x = 24
  
Action: Answer("C") The lake will be fully covered with water lilies after 24 doubling times, which takes 48 days.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  The number of water lilies on the lake doubles every two days.
  If it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies that started with 1 lily, then the lake is covered with $2^{30}$ lilies.
  If there were initially 64 lilies on the lake, then the number of days to fill the lake will be less than 30 days since 64 is less than $2^{6}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
If the number of water lilies doubled every two days, and we start with 1 water lily, then at the end of the first period of 2 days, there would be 2 water lilies. At the end of the second period of 2 days, there would be 4 water lilies and so on. Therefore, if it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies, then the number of times the number of water lilies doubles is 60/2 = 30 times.

If initially there were 64 water lilies, then after one doubling period (2 days), there will be 128 water lilies. In other words, the number of water lilies initially present is the same as the number of water lilies that would be present after one less doubling period. 

To get from 1 water lily to 64 water lilies, we need 6 fewer doubling periods than to get from 1 water lily to 2^30 water lilies. Therefore, the lake will be fully covered with water lilies in 30 - 6 = 24 doubling periods, or 24*2 = 48 days.
