### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 83 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Train M runs for 4 hours (5am-9am) from City A to City B.
  Train N runs for 3.5 hours (7am-10:30am) from City B to City A. 
  To find the time that the two trains cross each other, we can use the formula: 
    Total time taken by the two trains = Time taken by Train M + Time taken by Train N

Calculation:
  Let's assume that the two trains cross each other at X time, which is after 7 am.
  Therefore, the time taken by Train M to reach the crossing point is X - 5.
  Similarly, the time taken by Train N to reach the crossing point is 10:30 - X.
  Using the formula above, we can write: 
      X - 5 + 10:30 - X = 4 + 3.5
      5:30 = 7 - X 
      X = 7 - 5:30 = 1 hr 30 min

Answer:
  The two trains cross each other 1 hour and 30 minutes after 7 am which is 8:30 am.
  To calculate the time taken for the two trains to cross, we can subtract the time of the first train from the time of the crossing point or subtract the time of the second train from the time of the crossing point:
  The time taken by Train M to cross the point is 8:30 - 5:00 = 3 hours and 30 minutes.
  The time taken by Train N to cross the point is 10:30 - 8:30 = 2 hours. 
  Therefore, the two trains cross each other at 8:30 am and they take 3 hours and 30 minutes and 2 hours respectively to cross. 
  Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Train M takes 4 hours to travel from City A to City B.
  Train N takes 3 hours and 30 minutes to travel from City B to City A.
  The two trains will cross one another when the total distance covered by the two trains are the same as the distance between City A and City B.

Approach:
  Let's assume that the trains meet after x hours from 5 am when train M starts its journey. After x hours, train M would have covered a distance of 4x, and train N would have covered a distance of (3.5)(x-2) as it starts two hours later and arrives 2.5 hours later than train M.

  Since the distance from City A to City B is the same for both trains, we can set the two distances equal to each other and solve for x.

Calculation:
  4x = (3.5)(x-2) + 200
  4x = 3.5x - 7 + 200
  0.5x = 193
  x = 386/5

  Therefore, the two trains will meet after (386/5) hours from 5 am, which is approximately equal to 1 hour and 17 minutes.

  Total time elapsed from 5 am = 1 hour and 17 minutes + 2 hours = 3 hours and 17 minutes.
  Therefore, the two trains will meet at 8:17 am.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Let's solve the problem by finding the point in time when the distances covered by both trains are the same. We can start by finding the time it takes each train to travel the entire distance between A and B.
- Train M takes 4 hours (from 5am to 9am) to travel the distance from A to B.
- Train N takes 3.5 hours (from 7am to 10:30am) to travel the distance from B to A.

We know that Train M is on the track for two hours before Train N starts, which will make it reach a certain point before Train N. Let's find the distance covered by Train M before Train N starts:
- Train M traveled 4 hours * (1 hour/60 minutes) * 60 miles/hour = 240 miles in total.
- Train N traveled 3.5 hours * (1 hour/60 minutes) * 60 miles/hour = 210 miles in total.

Therefore, when Train N starts, it needs to travel 240 - 210 = 30 miles to meet Train M. Let x be the number of hours after 7 am when the two trains meet. In this amount of time, Train M would travel x + 2 hours, while Train N would travel x hours. As both trains are traveling towards each other,
x * (the speed of N) + (x+2) * (the speed of M) = 30 miles
Now, we can solve the equation to find x:
x * (v_N) + (x+2) * (v_M) = 30
x * (v_N) + x * (v_M) + 2 * (v_M) = 30
x * (v_N + v_M) = 28
x = 28 / (v_N + v_M)

We can calculate the average speed of the two trains:
- The distance from A to B is 240 miles, and the time for Train M to travel this distance is 4 hours. Therefore, Train M's speed is 240/4 = 60 miles per hour (mph).
- The distance from B to A is 240 miles, and the time for Train N to travel this distance is 3.5 hours. Therefore, Train N's speed is 240/3.5 = 68.57 mph (rounded to two decimal places).

Now we can calculate the time it takes for the two trains to meet each other:
x = 28 / (v_N + v_M) = 28 / (68.57 + 60) = 0.219 hours = 13.14 minutes

Therefore, the two trains will meet 13.14 minutes after 7 am, which is at 7:13:08 am (rounded to the nearest second). 

None of the choices in the question match this answer exactly, but the closest one is "B: 1 hr 15 min" which is equivalent to 1 hour 15 minutes * 60 minutes/hour = 75 minutes or 1 hour 15 minutes + 13 minutes (rounded seconds). Therefore, the closest choice to our answer is B.

Action: Answer("B")

  The two trains will cross when the distance travelled by Train M added to the distance travelled by Train N equals the total distance between the two cities.

Response 4:
Knowledge: 
  Train M takes 4 hours to reach City B from City A (5am to 9am)
  Train N takes 3.5 hours to reach City A from City B (7am to 10:30am)
  We need to calculate the time elapsed between when Train N departs City B and when the two trains meet.
  One way to approach this is to use the fact that in the time between Train N's departure and the time the two trains meet, Train M will have traveled for 2 hours (from 7am to 9am), while Train N will have traveled for 1.5 hours (from 7am to 8:30am).
  At the point where they meet, the two trains will have traveled a total distance equal to the sum of the distances they each traveled.
  We can set up an equation to solve for the time elapsed between Train N's departure and the time the two trains meet:
    (2 * speed of train M) + (1.5 * speed of train N) = distance between cities
  We know that the speeds of the two trains are constant, so we can solve for the time directly.
  We also know that the distance between the two cities is the same for both trains.
  
Calculation: 
  Let's assume that the speed of Train M is x and the speed of Train N is y. 
  At the point of crossing, the two trains will have traveled the same distance. Therefore:
  Distance covered by Train M = Distance covered by Train N
  Distance = Speed * Time
  Distance covered by Train M = Speed of Train M * (9 AM - 5 AM) = x * 4
  Distance covered by Train N = Speed of Train N * (10:30 AM - 7 AM) = y * 3.5
  x * 4 = y * 3.5
  (y / x) = (4/3.5)
  y = (4/3.5) * x
  Substituting value of y in first equation we get
  x * 4 = (4/3.5) * x * 3.5
  x = (4/3.5) * x
  x = 56/3 mph
  
  Distance = Speed * Time
  Distance covered by Train M = Speed of Train M * (9 AM - 5 AM) = (56/3) * 4
  Distance covered by Train N = Speed of Train N * (10:30 AM - 7 AM) = (4/3.5) * (3.5)
  Distance = Distance covered by Train M + Distance covered by Train N
  Distance = (56/3) * 4 + (4/3.5) * (3.5)
  Distance = 224/3 + 4
  Distance = 232/3
  Time = Distance / (Speed of Train M + Speed of Train N)
  Time = (232/3) / ((56/3) + (4/3.5))
  Time = 116 / (56 + 8/7)
  Time = 116 / (400/7)
  Time = 116 * 7 / 400
  Time = 2.02 hours = 2 hours and 1.2 minutes
  
  To find the time they cross, we need to add this elapsed time to the departure time of Train N:
  7:00 AM + 2:01 hours = 9:01 AM

Action: Answer("E")

Knowledge: We can solve this problem using the concept of distance, time and speed. We can assume that the trains meet at a distance x km from City A. We can then use the formula, speed = distance/time to solve the problem.  
Let's say the speed of train M is S1 km/hr and the speed of train N is S2 km/hr. We know that,
  Distance travelled by train M in 4 hours = x km
  Distance travelled by train N in 3.5 hours (i.e., from 7am to 10:30am) = x km
Therefore, we can write the equations:
  S1 x 4 = x     (Equation 1)
  S2 x 3.5 = x   (Equation 2)
We need to solve for x to find the distance at which the trains cross each other. Once we know the distance, we can find the time taken to cover that distance by each train and hence the total time. 
Action: Answer("A")  
Explanation: 
From Equation 1, we get x = 4S1
From Equation 2, we get x = 3.5S2
Equating the values of x from both equations, we get: 
  4S1 = 3.5S2
  S2 = (4/3.5)S1 = (8/7)S1
Let the time taken by train M to cover the distance x be t1 and the time taken by train N be t2. We know that: 
  t1 + t2 = 4  (since train M starts at 5am and reaches at 9am, it takes 4 hours)
  t1 - t2 = 2  (since train N starts at 7am and reaches at 10:30am, it takes 3.5 hours)
Solving these equations, we get: 
  t1 = 3 hr 4 min
  t2 = 57 min
Therefore, the trains cross each other 3 hours and 4 minutes after Train M leaves City A, i.e., at 8:04 am. So, the total time taken is 3 hr 4 min. 
Converting this into minutes, we get: 3 x 60 + 4 = 184 min 
The time taken is 184 - 60 = 124 min or 2 hr 4 min after Train N leaves City B, i.e., at 9:04am. 
Therefore, the time at which the two trains cross each other is 9:04am + 1 hr 23 min = 10:27am. 
Hence, the correct answer is (A) 1 hr 23 min.

  Train N takes 3 hours and 30 minutes to reach City A from City B.
  The two trains start heading towards each other at 9 am, two hours after Train M departs City A and two hours before Train N departs City B.
  
Calculation: 
  The time interval when both the trains are moving towards each other is 2 hours before Train N departs and 2 hours after Train M departs. This is a total of 4 hours.
  In the 4 hours, Train M travels a distance of 4/6 (since it takes 4 hours for Train M to cover 6 hours worth of distance between the two cities) of the distance between the two cities towards City B.
  On the other hand, Train B travels a distance of 3.5/6 of the distance between the two cities towards City A.
  Therefore, the total distance covered by both the trains towards each other is (4/6 + 3.5/6) of the distance between the two cities.
  Since the two trains move towards each other, their relative speed is the sum of their individual speeds.
  Therefore, the time taken by the two trains to cross each other is (Total Distance traveled towards each other) / (Relative Speed of the two trains)
  This is equal to [(4/6 + 3.5/6) * Distance between the two cities] / (Speed of Train M + Speed of Train N)
  = [(7.5/6) * Distance between the two cities] / (Speed of Train M + Speed of Train N)
  = [(5/4) * Distance between the two cities] / (Speed of Train M + Speed of Train N)

  We can assume that the two trains meet at a distance x km from City A, and both are traveling towards each other.
  We also know that Train M traveled for 4 hours and Train N traveled for 3.5 hours.
  The speed of Train M = x / 4
  The speed of Train N = x / 3.5
  The sum of their speeds = x / 4 + x / 3.5
  We know that their combined distance is the total distance between City A and City B, which is 4 + 3.5 = 7.5 hours.

  x / 4 + x / 3.5 = 7.5
  Multiplying both sides by 140 (4 x 3.5), we get:

  75x = 1050
  x = 14

  Train M travels from City A to City B in 4 hours (between 5 am and 9 am).
  Train N travels from City B to City A in 3.5 hours (between 7 am and 10:30 am).
  The trains meet each other when they are both traveling towards each other on the same track. 
  We can use the formula: Time = Distance / Speed

  Let us assume that the meeting point is X (somewhere between City A and City B).
  Let us assume that the distance between A and X be d1, and the distance between X and B be d2.
  Let us assume that the speed of Train M be s1, and the speed of Train N be s2.
  
  We can calculate d1 and d2 using the formula: Distance = Speed x Time.
  
  we can write: 
   d1 = s1 x t1   where t1 is the time taken by Train M to reach X from A. 
   d2 = s2 x t2   where t2 is the time taken by Train N to reach X from B. 

  We know that the total time of the meeting is 2 hours and that it occurred at X. 
  Therefore,
   t1 + t2 = 2
  
  We also know that the total distance traveled by the two trains is the same as the distance between A and B.
  Therefore, 
   d1 + d2 = Distance between A and B.

  Since Train M starts 2 hours before Train N, we can express t2 as follows: 
   t2 = t1 - 2
  
  Combining the equations, we get:
   d1 = s1 x t1
   d2 = s2 x (t1 - 2)
   d1 + d2 = Distance between A and B
  
  Plugging in the given values, we get:
   4s1 = d1 + d2
   3.5s2 = d1 + d2
   t1 + t2 = 2
   t2 = t1 - 2
  
  By substituting 4s1 and 3.5s2 for d1 + d2, and rearranging, we get:
   t1 = 14 / 3s = 4 hrs 40 mins
   
  Hence, the trains will cross each other at t1 + 2 or 6 hrs 40 mins after Train M started from City A, which is at 11:40 AM.
  
  We can verify the answer as follows: 
   Distance traveled by Train M = Speed of Train M x Time taken by Train M = s1 x t1 = 4s1.
   Distance traveled by Train N = Speed of Train N x Time taken by Train N = s2 x t2 = 3.5s2.
   Add the two distances together to see if they cover the entire distance between A and B.
   4s1 + 3.5s2 = Distance between A and B.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 84 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The formula for calculating average (arithmetic mean) is sum of all values divided by the total number of values.
  To solve this problem, we can use the formula: New Average = (Sum of original values + New value) / (Total number of values + 1)
  We know that the original average was 12.2 tons.
  We also know that there were 10 original values.
  We need to find the weight of the new value (the heavy duty truck).

Calculation:
  We can use algebra to solve for the weight of the new value:
  New Average = (Sum of original values + New value) / (Total number of values + 1)
  14.8 = (10 * 12.2 + New value) / 11
  14.8 * 11 = 10 * 12.2 + New value
  162.8 = 122 + New value
  New value = 162.8 - 122
  New value = 40.8
  
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The average (arithmetic mean) of a set of numbers is the sum of all the numbers divided by the total number of numbers.
  - If the average of a group of numbers increases by adding a new number, the sum of all the numbers must have increased by the value of the new number.
  - We can solve the problem using algebra if we let x be the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck.

Solution:
  Let's use algebra to solve for x:
  - The sum of the weights before the heavy duty truck was added was 10 * 12.2 = 122 tons.
  - The sum of the weights after the heavy duty truck was added is (10 * 12.2) + x = 122 + x.
  - The new average is (122 + x) / 11.
  - We are given that this new average is 2.6 tons higher than the old average, so we can set up the following equation:
    (122 + x) / 11 = 12.2 + 2.6
  - Solving for x:
    122 + x = 11 * 14.8
    122 + x = 162.8
    x = 40.8

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Let the average of the weight of 10 vehicles be x. Therefore, 10x = the sum of the weight of the 10 vehicles.
  After a new heavy duty truck was added, the average of the weight of 11 vehicles is x+2.6. The sum of the weight of the 11 vehicles is 11(x+2.6). 
  We can solve for the weight of the heavy duty truck using these 2 equations.
  The weight of the heavy duty truck would be the difference between the sum of the weight of the 11 vehicles and the sum of the weight of the 10 original vehicles.
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck would be (11(x+2.6)) - (10x).
  Simplifying this expression gives a weight of 28.6 tons.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 85 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Knowledge:
To solve this problem, we need to use the concept of alligation.

We can calculate that the amount of sand in the original mixture is:
10 kg x 30% = 3 kg.

Similarly, the amount of clay in the original mixture is:
10 kg x 70% = 7 kg.

Let x be the amount of mixture that is to be removed and replaced with pure sand.

After x kg of the original mixture is removed, the amount of sand left in the mixture is:
3 kg - (3/10) x = (30x - 3x)/100 = 27x/100.

Similarly, the amount of clay left in the mixture is:
7 kg - (7/10) x = (70x - 7x)/100 = 63x/100.

In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand, we need to find x such that:
27x/100 = 63x/100.

Solving for x, we get:
x = 30/7.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
Let's assume we have 10 kg of the mixture. That makes it 3 kg of sand and 7 kg of clay in the mixture.

We want to have an equal amount of sand and clay. In other words, we want 5 kg of each.

Let's assume we replace x kg of the mixture with pure sand. That means we remove x kg of the mixture.

Now, we have 3 kg of sand and (7-x) kg of clay in the mixture.

We need to add (5-3) = 2 kg of sand and remove (7-x-5) = (2-x) kg of clay.

So we have (3+x) kg of sand and (5-x) kg of clay after the replacement.

Therefore, we need to make sure that (3+x) = (5-x).

Solving the equation, we get x = 1.

So we need to remove 1 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.

Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  The perimeter of a rectangle is equal to the sum of all its sides.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot in this question is given as 340 metres. 
  The length of the rectangular plot is half of the perimeter minus twice the width: L = (340/2) - 2W. 
  The cost of gardening 1-metre boundary is calculated by finding the area of the rectangular plot subtracted by the area of the plot without the boundary, then multiplying by 10.
Action: 
  The width of the rectangular plot can be found by the formula for the perimeter of a rectangle: P = 2L + 2W. This means W = (P - 2L)/2 = (340 - 2L)/2 = 170 - L. Substituting the value of W into the L equation gives L = (340/2) - 2(170 - L) = 170 - L. Solving for L gives L = 85. 
  The area of the rectangular plot is L x W = 85 x (170 - 85) = 7225 square metres. 
  The area of the plot without the boundary is (L - 2) x (W - 2) = 83 x 168 = 13944 square metres.
  The area of the boundary is the difference between the two areas: 7225 - 13944 = 6721 square metres.
  The cost of gardening the 1-metre boundary is 6721 x 10 = 67210. 
  Therefore, the answer is A: 3400. 
  Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - The perimeter of a rectangle is the sum of the lengths of its four sides.
  - Let l be the length of the rectangle and w be the width of the rectangle.
  - Then, 2l + 2w = 340 (since the perimeter is 340)
  - That simplifies to l + w = 170
  - The cost of gardening 1-metre broad boundary around the rectangle equals the area of the 1-meter wide strip multiplied by the cost per square meter.
  - The area of the 1-meter wide strip equals the length of the rectangle plus twice the width of the rectangle (since there are two 1-meter strips on opposite sides). 
  - So, the area of the 1-meter wide strip is (l + 2w).
  - Therefore, the cost of gardening the 1-meter broad boundary equals 10 times (l + 2w).

Calculation:
  - From the knowledge above, we have l + w = 170.
  - Solving for l, we get l = 170 - w
  - Substituting into the area formula, we get area = (170 - w + 2w) = (170 + w)
  - Cost = area * 10 = 10(170 + w) = 1700 + 10w

Action: Answer("B") 
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  Perimeter of a rectangle = 2 (length + breadth)
  Let's say the length of the rectangular plot is l and the breadth is b.
  We have the equation 2(l + b) = 340, which can be simplified to l + b = 170.
  The cost of gardening 1 square meter of boundary is 10.

Calculation:
  We need to calculate the area of the rectangular plot first and then subtract the area of the inner rectangle (formed by reducing 1 meter from the sides of the rectangular plot) from it to get the area of the boundary.
    Area of rectangular plot = l * b
    Area of inner rectangle = (l - 2) * (b - 2)
    Area of the boundary = (l * b) - ((l - 2) * (b - 2)) = 2(l + b) - 4

  Since we know l + b = 170, we can substitute it in the above equation and get:
    Area of the boundary = 2(170) - 4 = 336 square meters
    Cost of gardening the boundary = 336 * 10 = 3360

Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  Perimeter of a rectangle can be calculated by adding the lengths of all four sides of the rectangle.
  A boundary around a rectangular plot can be represented as a rectangle with length and width equal to the respective sides of the original rectangular plot, plus one meter for each side.
  To find the cost of gardening the boundary, we need to find the area of the boundary and then multiply it by the given rate.

Calculation:
Let's assume the original rectangular plot has length L and width W.
Perimeter = 2(L + W) = 340
L + W = 170
The boundary around the rectangular plot will have length L+2 and width W+2 (since we are adding one meter on each side).
The area of the boundary can be calculated as:
(Boundary length) x (Boundary width) = (L+2) x (W+2)
Area of boundary = LW + 2L + 2W + 4

The cost of gardening the boundary will be:
Cost = (Area of boundary) x (Rate per square meter)
Cost = [(LW + 2L + 2W + 4) x 10]

  The area of the gardening required is (l+2)(b+2) - lb sq. meters.
  The cost of gardening will be the area of gardening multiplied by the rate of 10 per square meter.

=> l + b = 170
Let the cost of gardening be C.
The area of gardening required is (l+2)(b+2) - lb sq. meters.
=> area of gardening = lb + 2l + 2b + 4 sq. meters.
=> area of gardening = lb + 2(l+b) + 4 sq. meters.
=> area of gardening = lb + 2*170 + 4 sq. meters.
=> area of gardening = lb + 344 sq. meters.

Therefore, the cost of gardening will be C = (lb + 344) * 10.

  The perimeter of a rectangle with length L and width W is given by the formula P = 2(L+W).
  The cost of gardening a plot is the product of the area of the plot and the cost per square metre.
  The area of a rectangle with length L and width W is given by the formula A = LW.

Calculation:
  Let the length of the rectangular plot be L and the width be W.
  We know that P = 2(L+W) = 340.
  Solving for L+W, we get L+W = 170.
  We also know that the 1-metre boundary around the plot will add 2 metres to both the length and the width.
  Therefore, the new perimeter will be P_new = 2(L+2+W+2) = 2(L+W+4) = 2(170+4) = 348.
  We can now solve for L and W by using the system of equations:
  L+W = 170    (from P = 2(L+W) = 340)
  (L+2)(W+2) = A     (from adding the 1-metre boundary to both length and width)
  A = (L+2)(W+2) - LW   (since A is the area of the 1-metre boundary around the plot)
  Using substitution, we can solve for W:
  W = 170 - L
  A = [(L+2)(170 - L + 2)] - L(170 - L)
    = [(L+2)(172 - L)] - (170L - L^2)
    = -L^2 + 2L(174) - 172L + (2)(172)
    = -L^2 + 4L + 344
  Using the cost formula, the cost will be C = 10A
  C = 10(-L^2 + 4L + 344)
  C = -10L^2 + 40L + 3440

  Since we know the perimeter (340 m), we can write the equation: 2(length + width) = 340
  We are also given that the cost per square meter of gardening is 10.
  To find the area of the gardening boundary, we need to subtract the area of the rectangle from the area of the rectangle with the boundary. 
  The area of a rectangle is given by the formula: length x width.
Action:

  2(length + width) = 340
  length + width = 170
  width = 170 - length
  
  Now let's find the area of the rectangle:
  Area of rectangle = length x width
  Area of rectangle = length x (170 - length)
  Area of rectangle = 170length - length^2
  
  Now let's find the area of the larger rectangle with the boundary:
  Since the boundary is 1-metre broad around the rectangle, the new length and width will be (length + 2) and (width + 2) respectively.
  Area of larger rectangle = (length + 2) x (width + 2)
  Area of larger rectangle = (length + 2) x (170 - length + 2)
  Area of larger rectangle = (length + 2)(172 - length)
  Area of boundary = area of larger rectangle - area of rectangle
  Area of boundary = (length + 2)(172 - length) - (170length - length^2)
  Area of boundary = 344 - 2length
  
  Now let's find the cost of gardening the boundary:
  Cost = Area of boundary x Cost per square meter
  Cost = (344 - 2length) x 10
  Cost = 3440 - 20length

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
We can start the question by using algebra and setting variables for Joe's age, his sister's age, and his father's age. Let's say Joe's age is "J", his sister's age is "S", and his father's age is "F". Based on the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that when Joe is as old as his father (meaning J = F), his sister will be twice her current age (meaning S * 2). We can set up an equation using this information:

J + S + F = 100
(J + F) + S = S * 2

We can simplify the second equation by substituting J with F:

(F + F) + S = S * 2
2F + S = 2S
2F = S

Now we have two equations and two variables. We can substitute 2F for S in the first equation and solve for F:

J + S + F = 100
J + 2F + F = 100
J + 3F = 100
J = 100 - 3F

Substituting J with F again:

F = 100 - 3F
4F = 100
F = 25

Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 25. 

Action: Answer("None of the Above") 
Note: None of the above is the correct answer as the age of Joe's father is not listed as any of the choices.
Response 1:
Let:
  Joe's current age be J
  Joe's sister's current age be S
  Joe's father's current age be F
  
From the first sentence, we can form an equation:
  J + S + F = 100                                      Equation 1

From the second sentence, we can form another equation:
  J + (F-J) = F                                        Equation 2
  Solving for J, we get: J = F/2

From the third sentence, we can form another equation:
  (F-J) = 2*(S)                                         Equation 3
  Substituting J in Equation 3 from Equation 2:
  (F - F/2) = 2*(S) => F = 4S                                   
  
Substituting F = 4S in Equation 1:
  J + S + 4S = 100
  J + 5S = 100
  J = 100 - 5S

Substituting J and F in Equation 2:
  F/2 + (F-F/2) = F
  F = 2*(F/2)

Solving for F:
  F = 40

Therefore, Joe's father's current age is 40.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Let's use J for Joe's age, S for Joe's sister's age, and F for Joe's father's age.

From the first sentence, we know that:

J + S + F = 100

From the second sentence, we know that:

When J = F, S + (F - S) * 2 = 2S

Simplifying this equation: 

S + 2F - 2S = 2S

2F - S = S

2F = 2S + S

2F = 3S

From the third sentence, we know that:

When J = F, F = 2 * (S - F + J)

Simplifying this equation: 

F = 2S - 2F + 2J

3F = 2S + 2J

Using substitution, we can solve for F:

3F = 2S + 2J

3F = 2(2F - S) + 2(F - S + J)

3F = 4F - 2S + 2F - 2S + 2J

3F = 6F - 4S + 2J

3F = 4S + 2J

Substituting 2F = 3S into the equation:

3F = 4S + 2J

3F = 4(2F/3) + 2J

9F/3 = 8F/3 + 2J/3

F/3 = 2J/3

F = 2J

Substituting F = 2J into J + S + F = 100:

J + S + 2J = 100

3J + S = 100

Since we don't know Joe's age, we can make a reasonable assumption that Joe is between 20 and 30 years old. Let's start by assuming Joe is 25 years old:

3J + S = 100
3(25) + S = 100
S = 25

Now we can use J + S + F = 100 to solve for F:

J + S + F = 100
25 + 25 + F = 100
F = 50

Therefore, the answer is choice C: 50.
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
Let's assume, Joe's age = J, Joe's sister's age = S and Joe's father's age = F. 
From the question stem, we can gather the following information:
- J + S + F = 100
- When J = F, S+J = 2S (Joe's sister will be twice as old as now)
- When J = F, F = 2*(S-(F-J)) (Joe's father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father)

Action: 
Substitute the second equation in the third equation and simplify it to get F in terms of J. Then, substitute J+F-S=100 into the resulting equation. Finally, solve for F.

[(S-J)+J] = 2S
S-J = S/2

F = 2*(S-(F-J))
F = 2*S - 2*(F-J)
F = 2J + S

J+F-S = 100
J+(2J+S)-S = 100
3J = 100
J = 100/3

F = 2J + S
F = 2(100/3) + S

We don't know the age of Joe's sister, but we can solve for F in terms of S to eliminate J. 

S-J = S/2
S = 3J

F = 2(100/3) + S
F = 2(100/3) + 3J
F = 2(100/3) + 3(100/3)/3
F = 50

Answer: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Let the age of Joe, Joe's sister and Joe's father be J, S, and F, respectively. 

From the first sentence, we know that: 
J + S + F = 100 

From the second sentence, we know that:
J + (F-J) = F  (when Joe is as old as his father) 
S + (F-J) = 2S  (when Joe is as old as his father and Joe's sister is twice as old as now) 
=> S = F - J  (from the first equation)
=> S = F - 2(F-J) = -F + 2J  (substituting F-J with J)

From the third sentence, we know that:
F = 2(S - (F-S))
=> F = 3S - 2F
=> 3F = 3S
=> F = S 

Substituting S=F into S=F-2(F-J), we get:
F = -F + 2J
=> F = J/3

So the age of Joe's father is J/3. 

Substituting this into the first equation, we get:
J + S + F = 100 
=> J + F + F = 100
=> J + J/3 + J/3 = 100
=> J = 45

Therefore, the age of Joe's father is:
J/3 = 45/3 = 15 

Answer: Answer("A")
Response 5:
Let's denote Joe's current age as x, Joe's sister's current age as y, and Joe's father's current age as z.

From the first statement,  x + y + z = 100.

From the second statement, when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister's age will also have increased by that same amount of time. This means that Joe's sister's age will be y + (z - x) = 2y. Simplifying this equation gives z - x = y.

From the third statement, when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's father will be twice as old as when Joe's sister was as old as her father. This means that z + (z - x) = 2(y + x - z). Simplifying this equation gives z = 3x - y.

We now have two equations with two variables, which we can solve simultaneously:

x + y + z = 100  (equation 1)
z - x = y        (equation 2)
z = 3x - y       (equation 3)

Substituting equation 2 into equation 1 gives:

2z + y = 100

Substituting equation 3 into this gives:

2(3x - y) + y = 100

Simplifying this equation gives:

6x - y = 50

We now have two equations with two variables again:

z = 3x - y        (equation 3)
6x - y = 50       (equation 4)

Substituting equation 4 into equation 3 gives:

z = 3x - (6x - 50)
z = 50 - 3x

Substituting this equation into equation 1 gives:

x + y + 50 - 3x = 100
y - 2x = 50

We now have two equations with two variables again:

z = 50 - 3x       (equation 5)
y - 2x = 50       (equation 6)

Solving equation 6 for y gives:

y = 2x + 50

Substituting this into equation 5 gives:

z = 50 - 3x = 50 - 3(x)

Therefore, Joe's father's age is currently 50 - 3x.

F = 3S - J

F = 3F - J

Response 9:
Let J be Joe's age, S be Joe's sister's age and F be Joe's father's age. 
From the first sentence, we have J + S + F = 100. 

At the time when Joe is as old as his father (let's call this time T1), we have 
J + T1 = F + T1  -> J = F  (1)

At time T1, Joe's sister is twice as old as she is currently, so 
S + T1 = 2S -> T1 = S   (2)

Finally, at time T1, Joe's father is twice as old as Joe's sister was when she was the age Joe is now (let's call this time T2). So,
F + T1 = 2*(S - T2) -> F = 2S - 2T2 - T1 (3)

We now have three equations (1), (2), and (3) and three unknowns (J, S, F). We can use substitution to solve:
From (1), we have F = J.
Substituting this into (3), we get:
J = 2S - 2T2 - T1
J + S + J = 100
Substituting (2) into the above equation, we get:
J + (2T1) + J = 100
Substituting (1) into the above equation, we get:

3F + 2T1 = 100
Substituting (1) and (2) into the above equation, we get:

Substituting J = F = 25 into (2), we get:

T1 = S
25 + S + 25 = 100

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  If the coin landed on Heads h times and on Tails t times, then we can form two equations:
  h + t = 20    (The total number of tosses)
  2h - 3t = 0    (No money is won or lost)
  
  We can solve this system of equations to find the value of h.
  
Action: 
Substituting the second equation into the first, we get:
2h + 2t = 40
Adding this to the first equation, we get:
3h = 40
Therefore, h = 40/3
Since the number of tosses has to be an integer, the number of times the coin landed on Heads has to be a multiple of 3. The only multiple of 3 among the answer choices is 18. 
Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  - If the coin lands on heads, Christopher loses $2 and Jonathan gains $2.
  - If the coin lands on tails, Christopher gains $3 and Jonathan loses $3.
  - The total amount of money exchanged should be zero if none of them won or lost any amount.
Solution:
  Let's say the coin lands on heads x times and tails (20-x) times.
  Then, Christopher loses $2x and Jonathan gains $2x (because the coin landed on heads x times).
  Christopher gains $3(20-x) and Jonathan loses $3(20-x) (because the coin landed on tails 20-x times).
  If their total loss and gain is equal, then:
  2x = 3(20-x)
  5x = 60
  x = 12
Action: Answer("E")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  1. If a Head shows up, Christopher loses $2 and Jonathan gains $2.
  2. If a Tail shows up, Christopher gains $3 and Jonathan loses $3.
  3. After 20 coin flips, none of them won or lost any amount.
  4. The total amount Christopher loses is equal to the total amount Jonathan gains.
  5. The total amount Christopher gains is equal to the total amount Jonathan loses.

Let's assume that the number of times the coin landed on Heads is x.

Since the total number of coin flips is 20, the number of times it lands on Tails will be (20 - x).

If Christopher lost $2 x times and gained $3 (20 - x) times, then the total amount he gained is $3(20 - x) - $2x.

If Jonathan gained $2 x times and lost $3 (20 - x) times, then the total amount he lost is $3(20 - x) - $2x.

Since both of them neither gained nor lost any amount, the total amount Christopher gained must be equal to the total amount Jonathan lost.

Therefore, we can set up the equation:
$3(20 - x) - $2x = $2x - $3(20 - x)

Solving the equation gives us:
x = 10

Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Knowledge: 
  In each flip, there are two possibilities (heads or tails), and the result of each flip is independent of the previous flip.
  Christopher gives $2 for each head, and Jonathan gives $3 for each tail.
  After twenty times, there was no net gain or loss for either of them.
  
Solution:
  Let the number of heads be h and the number of tails be t. 
  We know that h + t = 20, since they flipped the coin twenty times.
  Also, Christopher gave $2 for each head, so he gave away 2h dollars in total. Jonathan gave $3 for each tail, so he gave away 3t dollars in total. Since they ended up with no net gain or loss, we have:
  2h - 3t = 0.
  We can rewrite this as:
  2h = 3t.
  Since the left-hand side is even and the right-hand side is odd, we know that both h and t must be even as well (otherwise, there would be no way to make the equation hold).
  The only even number among the answer choices is 10, so we can guess that h = 10 and t = 10.
  We can check that this works: Christopher gives away 20 dollars for the 10 heads, and Jonathan gives away 30 dollars for the 10 tails, so there is no net gain or loss.

Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. 
  Once he reached B, he turned around and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. 
  Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. 

Let's assume that the distance between A and B is x. We know that Kevin traveled half of that distance, and then turned around, so he traveled a total of x miles.
We know that the time he spent driving at 70 mph is equal to the time he spent driving at 90 mph, because he traveled the same distance each way. 

Let's call the time he spent driving at 70 mph "t" (in hours), and let's call the distance from B that he was 3 hours before the end of his trip "d" (in miles). 

Using the formula distance = rate x time, we can write two equations:
 
 70t + 90t = x   (where x is the distance between A and B)
 70t + 90(t-3) = d    (he was 70 miles away from B at time t-3)

We know that d=70, so we can substitute that into the second equation.

 70t + 90(t-3) = 70
 160t - 270 = 0
 t = 1.6875

Now we can substitute t into the first equation to find x.

 70t + 90t = x
 70(1.6875) + 90(1.6875) = x
 x = 270

Action: Answer("C")

  We can use the formula d = rt, where d is the distance, r is the rate or speed, and t is the time.
  Let us call the distance from A to B as d.
  Let us call the time it took for Kevin to get from A to B as t.
  Let us call the time it took for Kevin to get from B back to A (including his pause) as 3 + t
  Kevin drove 70 mph to go from A to B.
  Kevin drove 90 mph to go from B to A.
  We know that, 3 hours before the end of his trip, Kevin was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  At that point, Kevin has already completed the trip from A to B and was on his way back to A.
  So, he must have driven 70 miles since he left B.
  Therefore, the distance from A to B is (d - 70) miles.

Calculation:
  Time taken for Kevin to go from A to B = d / 70
  Time taken for Kevin to go from B to A (including his pause) = d / 90 + 3

  At the point when Kevin was 70 miles away from B:
  Distance Kevin drove from A to that point = d - 70
  Time taken by Kevin to drive that distance = (d - 70) / 90
  Time taken by Kevin to drive the remaining 70 miles = 70 / 70

  Total time taken by Kevin for the whole trip = (d / 70) + (d / 90) + 3

  We know that, 3 hours before the end of his trip, Kevin was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  Therefore, (d - 70) / 90 + 70 / 70 = (d / 70) + (d / 90) - 3
  Simplifying the equation, we get d = 360

Answer: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Knowledge: 
  To solve this problem, we can use the formula: Distance = Speed x Time.
  We can also use the formula: Time = Distance / Speed.
  Let's call the distance between A and B "d".
  Let's call the time it takes for Kevin to drive from A to B "t1".
  Let's call the time it takes for Kevin to drive from B to A "t2".
  We know that Kevin drove at a constant speed of 70 mph from A to B, and at a constant speed of 90 mph from B to A.
  We also know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. This is important because it tells us that he spent more time driving from B to A than from A to B.

Solution:
  Let's start by finding the time it took Kevin to drive from A to B (t1).
  We know that Distance1 = Speed1 x Time1.
  Distance1 = d
  Speed1 = 70
  Time1 = Distance1 / Speed1 = d / 70.
  
  Now, let's find the time it took Kevin to drive from B to A (t2).
  We know that Distance2 = Speed2 x Time2.
  Distance2 = d
  Speed2 = 90
  Time2 = Distance2 / Speed2 = d / 90.

  We also know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  Let's call the time it took Kevin to drive from the point where he was 70 miles away from B to B "t3".
  We know that Distance3 = Speed2 x Time3 (because he was driving from B to A at this point).
  Distance3 = 70
  Speed2 = 90
  Time3 = Distance3 / Speed2 = 70 / 90 = 7/9 hours.

  We also know that he had 3 hours left to complete his trip. This means that he had spent a total of t1 + t2 + t3 - 3 hours driving.
  t1 + t2 + t3 - 3 = t1 + t2
  t3 = 3

  Now we can set up an equation to solve for d:
  d = Distance1 + Distance2
  d = Speed1 x Time1 + Speed2 x Time2
  d = 70 x (d/70) + 90 x (d/90)
  d = d + (3/2)d
  d = 6d / 2
  d = 3 x 90
  d = 270.

Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Let's assume that the number of employees in the organization is 'x'.
Then, the contribution of each employee is Rs. (600000/x).
According to the question, if each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the new contribution of each employee would be Rs. [(600000 + 24000)/x] = Rs. [624000/x].
We can set up the equation as follows: 

[(600000/x) + 60]x = 624000

Simplifying the above equation, we get:

600000 + 60x = 624000

60x = 24000

x = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Let's assume that the number of employees in the organization is x.

So, according to the problem:
6 lakh/x + 60 = (6.24 lakh)/x
Solving this equation: 
x = 400
Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.

x*y = 6,00,000    ----(1)

Now the organization wants to raise an additional Rs. 24,000 (6,24,000 - 6,00,000) by collecting equal contributions from each employee. If each employee contributed Rs. 60 more, then the new contribution per employee would be (y + 60). The total amount raised by employees is now Rs. 6.24 lakh. We can form the following equation from this information:

x*(y+60) = 6,24,000   ----(2)

We can simplify equation (2) by expanding the expression:

xy + 60x = 6,24,000

Substituting the value of xy from equation (1):

6,00,000 + 60x = 6,24,000

60x = 24,000

x = 400

Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.

### Exam: aqua-rat-100 | Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Let the number be x.
  The value of 7/8 of the number = (7/8)*x
  The value of 7/18 of the number = (7/18)*x
  The error made by student = (7/8)*x - (7/18)*x = (35/72)*x
  It is given that (35/72)*x = 770, so x = (770*72)/35 = 1584
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  Let's assume the actual number is x. 
  To find 7/8 of x, we need to multiply x by 7/8 = 0.875
  To find 7/18 of x, we need to multiply x by 7/18 = 0.3889
  The difference between 0.875x and 0.3889x is equal to 770.

Calculation:
  0.875x - 0.3889x = 770
  0.4861x = 770
  x = 1584

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:

  The student found 7/18 of the number instead of 7/8, so we need to adjust the answer.
  The difference between 7/8 and 7/18 is 21/72, which reduces to 7/24.
  So the student actually found (7/18) / (7/24) = 4/9 of the number.

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Knowledge:
- The cost for the first quarter-mile is $3.50
- The cost for each additional quarter-mile beyond the first quarter-mile is $0.10
- $8.50 is the total amount of money we can spend on the cab ride.

Solution:
We can start by calculating how many quarter-miles we can travel with the initial $3.50:
$3.50 / $0.10 per quarter-mile = 35 quarter-miles

Then, we can calculate how many quarter-miles we can travel beyond the first quarter-mile with the remaining $5.00:
$5.00 / $0.10 per quarter-mile = 50 quarter-miles

Therefore, the total number of quarter-miles we can travel is:
35 + 50 = 85 quarter-miles

Finally, we can convert the total number of quarter-miles to miles:
85 quarter-miles * 0.25 miles per quarter-mile = 21.25 miles

However, we have to take into account that we only have $8.50, so we cannot travel the full 21.25 miles. Let's calculate the cost of a 21-mile ride:
The cost of the first quarter-mile is $3.50, and the cost of each quarter-mile for the remaining 20.75 miles is $0.10. So, the total cost of a 21-mile ride is:
$3.50 + ($0.10 x 83) = $12.30

Since we only have $8.50, we cannot travel 21 miles. We can calculate the maximum distance we can travel by finding the number of quarter-miles we can travel with the initial $3.50, and the number of additional quarter-miles we can travel with the remaining $5.00 minus the cost of the initial quarter-mile:
($8.50 - $3.50) / $0.10 per quarter-mile = 50 quarter-miles
50 quarter-miles + 1 initial quarter-mile = 51 quarter-miles
51 quarter-miles * 0.25 miles per quarter-mile = 12.75 miles

  We can find the maximum value of x using the total fare that we can afford.

  8.50 = 3.50 + 0.10x
  x = 50

  distance = ((8.50 - 3.50)/0.10)/4 + 0.25
  distance = 12.75 miles
